href="/wiki/.za" title=".za">.za</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>South Africa</b>, officially the <b>Republic of South Africa</b> (<b>RSA</b>), is the southernmost country in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. It is bounded to the south by 2,798 kilometres (1,739&#160;mi) of coastline of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a> stretching along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Atlantic" title="South Atlantic">South Atlantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Oceans</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-safacts_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-safacts-12">[11]</a></sup> to the north by the neighbouring countries of <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>; and to the east and northeast by <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini (Swaziland)</a>; and it surrounds the <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">enclaved country</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> South Africa is the largest country in Southern Africa and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">25th-largest country</a> in the world by land area and, with over <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_South_Africa" title="Demographics of South Africa">57 million people</a>, is the world\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" title="List of countries by population">24th-most populous nation</a>. It is the southernmost country on the mainland of the <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern Hemisphere</a>. About 80 percent of South Africans are of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a> ancestry,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cib11_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-cib11-6">[5]</a></sup> divided among a <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_South_Africa" title="Ethnic groups in South Africa">variety of ethnic groups</a> speaking <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">different African languages</a>, nine of which have official status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-safacts_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-safacts-12">[11]</a></sup> The remaining population consists of Africa\'s largest communities of <a href="/wiki/White_South_Africans" title="White South Africans">European (White)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_South_Africans" title="Asian South Africans">Asian</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indian_South_Africans" title="Indian South Africans">Indian</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Multiracial" title="Multiracial">multiracial</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coloured" title="Coloured">Coloured</a>) ancestry.\n</p><p>South Africa is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiethnic_society" title="Multiethnic society">multiethnic society</a> encompassing a wide <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_South_Africa" title="Culture of South Africa">variety of cultures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">languages</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_South_Africa" title="Religion in South Africa">religions</a>. Its pluralistic makeup is reflected in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">constitution</a>\'s recognition of 11 official languages, which is the fourth highest number in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-safacts_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-safacts-12">[11]</a></sup> Two of these languages are of European origin: <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> developed from <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> and serves as the first language of most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coloured" title="Coloured">coloured</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_South_African" title="White South African">white</a> South Africans; <a href="/wiki/South_African_English" title="South African English">English</a> reflects the legacy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_colonialism" title="British colonialism">British colonialism</a>, and is commonly used in public and commercial life, though it is fourth-ranked as a spoken <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-safacts_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-safacts-12">[11]</a></sup> The country is one of the few in Africa never to have had a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d\'&#233;tat">coup d\'&#233;tat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_South_Africa" title="Elections in South Africa">regular elections</a> have been held for almost a century. However, the vast majority of black South Africans were not <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enfranchised" title="Enfranchised">enfranchised</a> until 1994. During the 20th century, the black majority sought to recover its rights from the dominant white minority, with this struggle playing a large role in the country\'s recent <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Africa" title="History of South Africa">history</a> and politics. The <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">National Party</a> imposed <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> in 1948, institutionalising previous racial segregation. After a long and sometimes violent <a href="/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_apartheid" title="Internal resistance to apartheid">struggle</a> by the <a href="/wiki/African_National_Congress" title="African National Congress">African National Congress</a> (ANC) and other anti-apartheid activists both inside and outside the country, the repeal of discriminatory laws began in 1990.\n</p><p>Since 1994, all ethnic and linguistic groups have held political representation in the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democracy</a>, which comprises a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_South_Africa" title="Provinces of South Africa">nine provinces</a>. South Africa is often referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Rainbow_nation" title="Rainbow nation">rainbow nation</a>" to describe the country\'s multicultural diversity, especially in the wake of apartheid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> classifies South Africa as an upper-middle-income economy, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newly_industrialised_country" title="Newly industrialised country">newly industrialised country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waugh2000_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Waugh2000-16">[15]</a></sup> Its economy is the second-largest in Africa, and the 34th-largest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf2_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-7">[6]</a></sup> In terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>, South Africa has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">seventh-highest per capita income</a> in Africa. However, poverty and <a href="/wiki/Inequality_in_post-apartheid_South_Africa" title="Inequality in post-apartheid South Africa">inequality</a> remain widespread, with about a quarter of the population unemployed and living on less than US$1.25 a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> Nevertheless, South Africa has been identified as a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> in international affairs, and maintains significant regional influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lynch2010_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lynch2010-20">[19]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Name"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Name</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span archaeology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Bantu_expansion"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bantu expansion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Biodiversity"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Biodiversity</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#Animals"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Animals</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#Fungi"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Fungi</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#Plants"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Plants</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Conservation_issues"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Conservation issues</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Politics_and_government"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Politics and government</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Law"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Law</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Foreign_relations"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Foreign relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Military"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Military</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Administrative_divisions"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Administrative divisions</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Labour_market"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Labour market</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Science_and_technology"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Science and technology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Water_supply_and_sanitation"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Water supply and sanitation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Urban_centres"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Urban centres</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Religions"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Religions</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Arts"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Arts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Popular_culture"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Popular culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#HIV/AIDS"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">HIV/AIDS</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Official_names_of_South_Africa" title="Official names of South Africa">Official names of South Africa</a></div>\n<p>The name "South Africa" is derived from the country\'s geographic location at the southern tip of Africa. Upon formation, the country was named the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> in English, reflecting its origin from the unification of four formerly separate British colonies. Since 1961, the long form name in English has been the "Republic of South Africa". In Dutch, the country was named <i>Republiek van Zuid-Afrika</i>, replaced in 1983 by the <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> <i>Republiek van Suid-Afrika</i>. Since 1994, the Republic has had an official name in each of its <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">11 official languages</a>.\n</p><p><i>Mzansi</i>, derived from the <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> noun <i>umzantsi</i> meaning "south", is a <a href="/wiki/Colloquialism" title="Colloquialism">colloquial name</a> for South Africa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> while some <a href="/wiki/Pan-Africanism" title="Pan-Africanism">Pan-Africanist</a> political parties prefer the term "<a href="/wiki/Azania" title="Azania">Azania</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Africa" title="History of South Africa">History of South Africa</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_archaeology">Prehistoric archaeology</span></h3>\n<p>South Africa contains some of the oldest archaeological and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_fossil" title="Human fossil">human-fossil</a> sites in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Archaeologists have recovered extensive <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">fossil</a> remains from a series of caves in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauteng_Province" title="Gauteng Province">Gauteng Province</a>. The area, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a>, has been branded "the <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_Humankind" title="Cradle of Humankind">Cradle of Humankind</a>". The sites include <a href="/wiki/Sterkfontein" title="Sterkfontein">Sterkfontein</a>, one of the richest sites for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hominin" title="Hominin">hominin</a> fossils in the world. Other sites include <a href="/wiki/Swartkrans" title="Swartkrans">Swartkrans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gondolin_Cave" title="Gondolin Cave">Gondolin Cave</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kromdraai" title="Kromdraai">Kromdraai</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coopers_Cave" title="Coopers Cave">Coopers Cave</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malapa" title="Malapa">Malapa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Dart" title="Raymond Dart">Raymond Dart</a> identified the first hominin fossil discovered in Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Taung_Child" title="Taung Child">Taung Child</a> (found near <a href="/wiki/Taung" title="Taung">Taung</a>) in 1924. Further hominin remains have come from the sites of <a href="/wiki/Makapansgat" title="Makapansgat">Makapansgat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Limpopo" title="Limpopo">Limpopo Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornelia,_Free_State" title="Cornelia, Free State">Cornelia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florisbad" title="Florisbad">Florisbad</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_State_(South_African_province)" title="Free State (South African province)">Free State Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Border_Cave" title="Border Cave">Border Cave</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal_Province" title="KwaZulu-Natal Province">KwaZulu-Natal Province</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Klasies_River_Mouth" title="Klasies River Mouth">Klasies River Mouth</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape_Province" title="Eastern Cape Province">Eastern Cape Province</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pinnacle_Point" title="Pinnacle Point">Pinnacle Point</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elandsfontein_cranium" title="Elandsfontein cranium">Elandsfontein</a> and Die Kelders Cave in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Cape_Province" title="Western Cape Province">Western Cape Province</a>.\n</p><p>These finds suggest that various hominid species existed in South Africa from about three million years ago, starting with <i><a href="/wiki/Australopithecus_africanus" title="Australopithecus africanus">Australopithecus africanus</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> There followed species including <i><a href="/wiki/Australopithecus_sediba" title="Australopithecus sediba">Australopithecus sediba</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_ergaster" title="Homo ergaster">Homo ergaster</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_rhodesiensis" title="Homo rhodesiensis">Homo rhodesiensis</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_helmei" title="Homo helmei">Homo helmei</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_naledi" title="Homo naledi">Homo naledi</a></i> and modern humans (<i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i>). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_humans" title="Modern humans">Modern humans</a> have <a href="/wiki/Pinnacle_Point" title="Pinnacle Point">inhabited Southern Africa</a> for at least 170,000 years.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="460" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg/220px-South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg/330px-South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg/440px-South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_-_population_migrations.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Migrations that formed the modern <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_nation" title="Rainbow nation">Rainbow nation</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Various researchers have located <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pebble_tool" title="Pebble tool">pebble tools</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Vaal_River" title="Vaal River">Vaal River</a> valley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langer_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Langer-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bantu_expansion">Bantu expansion</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MapungubweHill.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/MapungubweHill.jpg/220px-MapungubweHill.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/MapungubweHill.jpg/330px-MapungubweHill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/MapungubweHill.jpg/440px-MapungubweHill.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MapungubweHill.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mapungubwe_Hill" title="Mapungubwe Hill">Mapungubwe Hill</a>, the site of the former capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mapungubwe" title="Kingdom of Mapungubwe">Kingdom of Mapungubwe</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Settlements of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu-speaking_peoples_of_South_Africa" title="Bantu-speaking peoples of South Africa">Bantu-speaking peoples</a>, who were iron-using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agriculturists" title="Agriculturists">agriculturists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herder" title="Herder">herdsmen</a>, were already present south of the <a href="/wiki/Limpopo_River" title="Limpopo River">Limpopo River</a> (now the northern border with Botswana and Zimbabwe) by the 4th or 5th century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_Era" title="Current Era">CE</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a>). They displaced, conquered and absorbed the original <a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">Khoisan</a> speakers, the <a href="/wiki/Khoikhoi" title="Khoikhoi">Khoikhoi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bushmen" title="Bushmen">San</a> peoples. The Bantu slowly moved south. The earliest <a href="/wiki/Ironworks" title="Ironworks">ironworks</a> in modern-day KwaZulu-Natal Province are believed to date from around 1050. The southernmost group was the <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_people" title="Xhosa people">Xhosa people</a>, whose language incorporates certain linguistic traits from the earlier Khoisan people. The Xhosa reached the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fish_River" title="Great Fish River">Great Fish River</a>, in today\'s Eastern Cape Province. As they migrated, these larger <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> populations displaced or assimilated earlier peoples.\nIn <a href="/wiki/Mpumalanga" title="Mpumalanga">Mpumalanga Province</a>, several stone circles have been found along with the stone arrangement that has been named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adam%27s_Calendar" title="Adam\'s Calendar">Adam\'s Calendar</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_contacts">Portuguese contacts</span></h3>\n<p>At the time of European contact, the dominant ethnic group were Bantu-speaking peoples who had migrated from other parts of Africa about one thousand years before. The two major historic groups were the Xhosa and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_people" title="Zulu people">Zulu peoples</a>.\n</p><p>In 1487, the Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> led the first European voyage to land in southern Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-domville-25_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-domville-25-30">[29]</a></sup> On 4 December, he landed at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walfisch_Bay" title="Walfisch Bay">Walfisch Bay</a> (now known as <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> in present-day Namibia). This was south of the furthest point reached in 1485 by his predecessor, the Portuguese navigator <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo C&#227;o">Diogo C&#227;o</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cape_Cross" title="Cape Cross">Cape Cross</a>, north of the bay). Dias continued down the western coast of southern Africa. After 8 January 1488, prevented by storms from proceeding along the coast, he sailed out of sight of land and passed the southernmost point of Africa without seeing it. He reached as far up the eastern coast of Africa as, what he called, <i>Rio do Infante</i>, probably the present-day <a href="/wiki/Groot_River_(Eastern_Cape)" title="Groot River (Eastern Cape)">Groot River</a>, in May 1488, but on his return he saw the Cape, which he first named <i>Cabo das Tormentas</i> (Cape of Storms). His King, <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">John II</a>, renamed the point <i>Cabo da Boa Esperan&#231;a</i>, or <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, as it led to the riches of the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> Dias\' feat of navigation was later immortalised in <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Lu&#237;s de Cam&#245;es">Lu&#237;s de Cam&#245;es</a>\' Portuguese epic poem, <i><a href="/wiki/Os_Lus%C3%ADadas" title="Os Lus&#237;adas">The Lusiads</a></i> (1572).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_colonisation">Dutch colonisation</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony" title="Dutch Cape Colony">Dutch Cape Colony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boer_Republics" title="Boer Republics">Boer Republics</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="748" data-file-width="989" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg/220px-Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg/330px-Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg/440px-Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_Davidson_Bell" title="Charles Davidson Bell">Charles Davidson Bell</a>\'s 19th-century painting of <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck" title="Jan van Riebeeck">Jan van Riebeeck</a>, who founded the first European settlement in South Africa, arrives in <a href="/wiki/Table_Bay" title="Table Bay">Table Bay</a> in 1652</div></div></div>\n<p>By the early 17th century, Portugal\'s maritime power was starting to decline, and English and Dutch merchants competed to oust Lisbon from its lucrative monopoly on the spice trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pakeman_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pakeman-32">[31]</a></sup> Representatives of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> did call sporadically at the Cape in search of provisions as early as 1601, but later came to favour <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Island" title="Ascension Island">Ascension Island</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Helena" title="St. Helena">St. Helena</a> as alternative ports of refuge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaap_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kaap-33">[32]</a></sup> Dutch interest was aroused after 1647, when two employees of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie" title="Verenigde Oostindische Compagnie">VOC</a>) were shipwrecked there for several months. The sailors were able to survive by obtaining fresh water and meat from the natives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaap_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kaap-33">[32]</a></sup> They also sowed vegetables in the fertile soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zastudy_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-zastudy-34">[33]</a></sup> Upon their return to Holland, they reported favourably on the Cape\'s potential as a "warehouse and garden" for provisions to stock passing ships for long voyages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaap_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kaap-33">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1652, a century and a half after the discovery of the Cape sea route, <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck" title="Jan van Riebeeck">Jan van Riebeeck</a> established a <i lang="en"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/victual#English" title="wikt:victual">victualling</a></i> station at the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, at what would become <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, on behalf of the Dutch East India Company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hunt1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hunt1-36">[35]</a></sup> In time, the Cape became home to a large population of <i>"vrijlieden"</i>, also known as <i>"vrijburgers"</i> (<abbr title="literal translation">lit.</abbr> free citizens), former Company employees who stayed in Dutch territories overseas after serving their contracts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hunt1_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hunt1-36">[35]</a></sup> Dutch traders also imported thousands of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a> to the fledgling colony from <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, and parts of eastern Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Worden_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Worden-37">[36]</a></sup> Some of the earliest mixed race communities in the country were formed through unions between <i>vrijburgers</i>, their slaves, and various indigenous peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zimstudy_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-zimstudy-38">[37]</a></sup> This led to the development of a new ethnic group, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Coloured" title="Cape Coloured">Cape Coloureds</a>, most of whom adopted the Dutch language and Christian faith.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zimstudy_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-zimstudy-38">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The eastward expansion of Dutch colonists ushered in a series of wars with the southwesterly migrating Xhosa tribe, known as the <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_Wars" title="Xhosa Wars">Xhosa Wars</a>, as both sides competed for the pastureland necessary to graze their cattle near the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fish_River" title="Great Fish River">Great Fish River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2-39">[38]</a></sup> <i>Vrijburgers</i> who became independent farmers on the frontier were known as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boers" title="Boers">Boers</a></i>, with some adopting semi-nomadic lifestyles being denoted as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trekboers" title="Trekboers">trekboers</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2-39">[38]</a></sup> The Boers formed loose <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militias</a>, which they termed <i>commandos</i>, and forged alliances with Khoisan groups to repel Xhosa raids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2-39">[38]</a></sup> Both sides launched bloody but inconclusive offensives, and sporadic violence, often accompanied by livestock theft, remained common for several decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2_39-3"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2-39">[38]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colonisation">British colonisation</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_the_Cape_Colony" title="Invasion of the Cape Colony">Invasion of the Cape Colony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Bechuanaland" title="British Bechuanaland">British Bechuanaland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Natal" title="Colony of Natal">Colony of Natal</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> occupied Cape Town between 1795 and 1803 to prevent it from falling under the control of the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">French First Republic</a>, which had invaded the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2_39-4"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2-39">[38]</a></sup> Despite briefly returning to Dutch rule under the <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Batavian Republic</a> in 1803, the Cape was occupied again by the British in 1806.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keegan_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keegan-40">[39]</a></sup> Following the end of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, it was formally ceded to Great Britain and became an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd1_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd1-41">[40]</a></sup> British immigration to South Africa began around 1818, subsequently culminating in the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/1820_Settlers" title="1820 Settlers">1820 Settlers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd1_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd1-41">[40]</a></sup> The new colonists were induced to settle for a variety of reasons, namely to increase the size of the European workforce and to bolster frontier regions against Xhosa incursions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd1_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd1-41">[40]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1087" data-file-width="1376" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg/220px-Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg/330px-Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg/440px-Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bell_-_Zoeloe-aanval_op_%27n_Boerelaer_-_1838.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depiction of a <a href="/wiki/Weenen_massacre" title="Weenen massacre">Zulu attack</a> on a Boer camp in February 1838</div></div></div>\n<p>In the first two decades of the 19th century, the Zulu people grew in power and expanded their territory under their leader, <a href="/wiki/Shaka" title="Shaka">Shaka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Shaka\'s warfare indirectly led to the <a href="/wiki/Mfecane" title="Mfecane">Mfecane</a> ("crushing"), in which 1,000,000 to 2,000,000 people were killed and the inland plateau was devastated and depopulated in the early 1820s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> An offshoot of the Zulu, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ndebele_people" title="Northern Ndebele people">Matabele</a> people created a larger empire that included large parts of the <a href="/wiki/Highveld" title="Highveld">highveld</a> under their king <a href="/wiki/Mzilikazi" title="Mzilikazi">Mzilikazi</a>.\n</p><p>During the early 1800s, many Dutch settlers departed from the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>, where they had been subjected to British control. They migrated to the future <a href="/wiki/Natal_(province)" title="Natal (province)">Natal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_Free_State" title="Orange Free State">Orange Free State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_(province)" title="Transvaal (province)">Transvaal</a> regions. The Boers founded the <a href="/wiki/Boer_Republics" title="Boer Republics">Boer Republics</a>: the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">South African Republic</a> (now Gauteng, Limpopo, Mpumalanga and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_West_Province_(South_Africa)" title="North West Province (South Africa)">North West</a> provinces), the <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Republic" title="Natalia Republic">Natalia Republic</a> (KwaZulu-Natal), and the Orange Free State (Free State).\n</p><p>The discovery of diamonds in 1867 and gold in 1884 in the interior started the <a href="/wiki/Mineral_Revolution" title="Mineral Revolution">Mineral Revolution</a> and increased economic growth and <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>. This intensified British efforts to gain control over the indigenous peoples. The struggle to control these important economic resources was a factor in relations between Europeans and the indigenous population and also between the Boers and the British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Zulu_War" title="Anglo-Zulu War">Anglo-Zulu War</a> was fought in 1879 between the British Empire and the Zulu Kingdom. Following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Carnarvon" title="Lord Carnarvon">Lord Carnarvon</a>\'s successful introduction of <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">federation in Canada</a>, it was thought that similar political effort, coupled with military campaigns, might succeed with the African kingdoms, tribal areas and Boer republics in South Africa. In 1874, Sir <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bartle_Frere" title="Henry Bartle Frere">Henry Bartle Frere</a> was sent to South Africa as <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_for_Southern_Africa" title="High Commissioner for Southern Africa">High Commissioner</a> for the British Empire to bring such plans into being. Among the obstacles were the presence of the independent states of the Boers and the <a href="/wiki/Zulu_Kingdom" title="Zulu Kingdom">Kingdom of Zululand</a> and its army. The Zulu nation defeated the British at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Isandlwana" title="Battle of Isandlwana">Battle of Isandlwana</a>. Eventually, though, the war was lost, resulting in the termination of the Zulu nation\'s independence.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boers_1881.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="401" data-file-width="380" decoding="async" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Boers_1881.png/220px-Boers_1881.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Boers_1881.png/330px-Boers_1881.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Boers_1881.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boers_1881.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boer" title="Boer">Boers</a> in combat (1881)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Boer_Republics" title="Boer Republics">Boer Republics</a> successfully resisted British encroachments during the <a href="/wiki/First_Boer_War" title="First Boer War">First Boer War</a> (1880&#8211;1881) using <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a> tactics, which were well suited to local conditions. The British returned with greater numbers, more experience, and new strategy in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a> (1899&#8211;1902) but suffered heavy casualties through <a href="/wiki/Attrition_warfare" title="Attrition warfare">attrition</a>; nonetheless, they were ultimately successful.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h4>\n<p>Within the country, anti-British policies among white South Africans focused on independence. During the Dutch and British colonial years, <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">racial segregation</a> was mostly informal, though some legislation was enacted to control the settlement and movement of native people, including the <a href="/wiki/Native_Location_Act_of_1879" title="Native Location Act of 1879">Native Location Act of 1879</a> and the system of <a href="/wiki/Pass_laws" title="Pass laws">pass laws</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Eight years after the end of the Second Boer War and after four years of negotiation, an act of the British Parliament (<a href="/wiki/South_Africa_Act_1909" title="South Africa Act 1909">South Africa Act 1909</a>) granted nominal independence, while creating the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> on 31 May 1910. The Union was a <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominion</a> that included the former territories of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_Colony" title="Transvaal Colony">Transvaal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Natal" title="Colony of Natal">Natal</a> colonies, as well as the Orange Free State republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natives%27_Land_Act" title="Natives\' Land Act">Natives\' Land Act</a> of 1913 severely restricted the ownership of land by blacks; at that stage natives controlled only 7% of the country. The amount of land reserved for <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> was later marginally increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1931, the union was fully sovereign from the United Kingdom with the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster</a>, which abolished the last powers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Government" title="British Government">British Government</a> on the country. In 1934, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Party" title="South African Party">South African Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">National Party</a> merged to form the <a href="/wiki/United_Party_(South_Africa)" title="United Party (South Africa)">United Party</a>, seeking reconciliation between Afrikaners and English-speaking whites. In 1939, the party split over the entry of the Union into <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_South_Africa_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of South Africa during World War II">ally of the United Kingdom</a>, a move which the National Party followers strongly opposed.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginning_of_apartheid">Beginning of apartheid</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="609" data-file-width="665" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg/220px-ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg/330px-ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg/440px-ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ApartheidSignEnglishAfrikaans.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"For use by white persons"&#160;&#8211; apartheid sign in English and <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1948, the National Party was elected to power. It strengthened the racial segregation begun under Dutch and British colonial rule. Taking <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Indian_Act" title="Indian Act">Indian Act</a> as a framework,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalist</a> government classified all peoples into three races and developed rights and limitations for each. The white minority (less than 20%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> controlled the vastly larger black majority. The legally institutionalized segregation became known as <i><a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a></i>. While whites enjoyed the highest <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a> in all of Africa, comparable to <a href="/wiki/First_World" title="First World">First World</a> Western nations, the black majority remained disadvantaged by almost every standard, including income, education, housing, and life expectancy. The <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Charter" title="Freedom Charter">Freedom Charter</a>, adopted in 1955 by the <a href="/wiki/Congress_Alliance" title="Congress Alliance">Congress Alliance</a>, demanded a non-racial society and an end to discrimination.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic">Republic</span></h3>\n<p>On 31 May 1961, the country became a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_republic_referendum,_1960" title="South African republic referendum, 1960">a referendum</a> in which white voters narrowly voted in favour thereof (the British-dominated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natal_Province" title="Natal Province">Natal</a> province rallied against the issue).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> was stripped of the title <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_of_South_Africa" title="Queen of South Africa">Queen of South Africa</a>, and the last <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Union_of_South_Africa" title="Governor-General of the Union of South Africa">Governor-General</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Robberts_Swart" title="Charles Robberts Swart">Charles Robberts Swart</a>, became <a href="/wiki/State_President_of_South_Africa" title="State President of South Africa">State President</a>. As a concession to the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>, the presidency remained parliamentary-appointed and virtually powerless until <a href="/wiki/P._W._Botha" title="P. W. Botha">P. W. Botha</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/South_African_Constitution_of_1983" title="South African Constitution of 1983">Constitution Act of 1983</a>, which eliminated the office of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_South_Africa" title="Prime Minister of South Africa">Prime Minister</a> and instated a near-unique "strong presidency" <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentarianism" title="Parliamentarianism">responsible to parliament</a>. Pressured by other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> countries, South Africa withdrew from the organisation in 1961, and rejoined it only in 1994.\n</p><p>Despite <a href="/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_apartheid" title="Internal resistance to apartheid">opposition</a> both within and outside the country, the government legislated for a continuation of apartheid. The security forces cracked down on internal dissent, and violence became widespread, with anti-apartheid organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/African_National_Congress" title="African National Congress">African National Congress</a> (ANC), the <a href="/wiki/Azanian_People%27s_Organisation" title="Azanian People\'s Organisation">Azanian People\'s Organisation</a> (AZAPO), and the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Africanist_Congress_of_Azania" title="Pan Africanist Congress of Azania">Pan-Africanist Congress</a> (PAC) carrying out guerrilla warfare<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biko1_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biko1-56">[55]</a></sup> and urban <a href="/wiki/Sabotage" title="Sabotage">sabotage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Switzer_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Switzer-57">[56]</a></sup> The three rival resistance movements also engaged in occasional inter-factional clashes as they jockeyed for domestic influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitchell_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mitchell-58">[57]</a></sup> Apartheid became increasingly controversial, and several countries began to <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycott</a> business with the South African government because of its racial policies. These measures were later extended to <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions" title="International sanctions">international sanctions</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Disinvestment_from_South_Africa" title="Disinvestment from South Africa">divestment of holdings</a> by foreign investors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bridgland_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bridgland-59">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Landgren_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Landgren-60">[59]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg/220px-Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg/330px-Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg/440px-Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frederik_de_Klerk_with_Nelson_Mandela_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_1992.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/F._W._de_Klerk" title="F. W. de Klerk">FW de Klerk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> shake hands in January 1992</div></div></div>\n<p>In the late 1970s, South Africa <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="South Africa and weapons of mass destruction">initiated a programme of nuclear weapons development</a>. In the following decade, it produced six deliverable nuclear weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_apartheid">End of apartheid</span></h4>\n<table class="box-Multiple_issues plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-multiple_issues compact-ambox" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" decoding="async" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><div class="mw-collapsible" it</a></b> or discuss these issues on the <b><a href="/wiki/Talk:South_Africa" title="Talk:South Africa">talk page</a></b>. <small><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove these template messages</a>)</i></small>\n<div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="margin-top: 0.3em;">\n<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png"
