<b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=South_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahlabatini_Declaration" title="Mahlabatini Declaration">Mahlabatini Declaration</a> of Faith, signed by <a href="/wiki/Mangosuthu_Buthelezi" title="Mangosuthu Buthelezi">Mangosuthu Buthelezi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Schwarz" title="Harry Schwarz">Harry Schwarz</a> in 1974, enshrined the principles of peaceful transition of power and equality for all, the first of such agreements by black and white political leaders in South Africa. Ultimately, <a href="/wiki/F._W._de_Klerk" title="F. W. de Klerk">FW de Klerk</a> opened bilateral discussions with <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> in 1993 for a transition of policies and government.\n</p><p>In 1990, the National Party government took the first step towards dismantling discrimination when it lifted the ban on the ANC and other political organisations. It released Nelson Mandela from prison after 27 years\' serving a sentence for sabotage. A <a href="/wiki/Negotiations_to_end_apartheid_in_South_Africa" title="Negotiations to end apartheid in South Africa">negotiation process</a> followed. With approval from the white electorate in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_apartheid_referendum,_1992" title="South African apartheid referendum, 1992">1992 referendum</a>, the government continued negotiations to end apartheid. South Africa also destroyed its nuclear arsenal and acceded to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a>. South Africa held its first universal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_general_election,_1994" title="South African general election, 1994">elections in 1994</a>, which the ANC won by an overwhelming majority. It has been in power ever since. The country rejoined the Commonwealth of Nations and became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Mandela-2008_(edit).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="778" data-file-width="657" decoding="async" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Nelson_Mandela-2008_%28edit%29.jpg/200px-Nelson_Mandela-2008_%28edit%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Nelson_Mandela-2008_%28edit%29.jpg/300px-Nelson_Mandela-2008_%28edit%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Nelson_Mandela-2008_%28edit%29.jpg/400px-Nelson_Mandela-2008_%28edit%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Mandela-2008_(edit).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>, first black African <a href="/wiki/President_of_South_Africa" title="President of South Africa">President of Republic of South Africa</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-apartheid_South_Africa" title="Post-apartheid South Africa">post-apartheid South Africa</a>, unemployment has been extremely high as the country has struggled with many changes. While many blacks have risen to middle or upper classes, the overall unemployment rate of black people worsened between 1994 and 2003 by official metrics, but declined significantly using expanded definitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sach3_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-sach3-63">[62]</a></sup> Poverty among whites, previously rare, increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> In addition, the current government has struggled to achieve the monetary and fiscal discipline to ensure both redistribution of wealth and economic growth. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN) <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) of South Africa fell from 1995 to 2005, while it was steadily rising until the mid-1990s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> before recovering its 1995 peak in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> This is in large part attributable to the <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_South_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS in South Africa">South African HIV/AIDS pandemic</a> which saw South African life expectancy fall from a high point of 62.25 years in 1992 to a low of 52.57 in 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> and the failure of the government to take steps to address it in the early years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2008, riots left over 60 people dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Broke-on-Broke_Violence_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Broke-on-Broke_Violence-69">[68]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Centre_on_Housing_Rights_and_Evictions" title="Centre on Housing Rights and Evictions">Centre on Housing Rights and Evictions</a> estimates over 100,000 people were driven from their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> The targets were mainly <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_South_Africa" title="Immigration to South Africa">legal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_South_Africa" title="Illegal immigration to South Africa">illegal migrants</a> and refugees seeking asylum, but a third of the victims were South African citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Broke-on-Broke_Violence_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Broke-on-Broke_Violence-69">[68]</a></sup> In a 2006 survey, the South African Migration Project concluded that South Africans are more opposed to immigration than anywhere else in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UN High Commissioner for Refugees</a> in 2008 reported over 200,000 refugees applied for asylum in South Africa, almost four times as many as the year before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-72">[71]</a></sup> These people were mainly from <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, though many also come from <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-72">[71]</a></sup> Competition over jobs, business opportunities, public services and housing has led to tension between refugees and host communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-72">[71]</a></sup> While <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">xenophobia</a> is still a problem, recent violence has not been as widespread as initially feared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_72-3"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-72">[71]</a></sup> Nevertheless, as South Africa continues to grapple with racial issues, one of the proposed solutions has been to pass legislation, such as the pending <a href="/wiki/The_Prevention_and_Combating_of_Hate_Crimes_and_Hate_Speech_Bill" title="The Prevention and Combating of Hate Crimes and Hate Speech Bill">Hate Crimes and Hate Speech Bill</a>, to uphold South Africa\'s ban on racism and commitment to equality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_South_Africa" title="Geography of South Africa">Geography of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6756" data-file-width="9960" decoding="async" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg/300px-Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg/450px-Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg/600px-Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Southern_African_Central_Plateau.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of South Africa showing the main topographic features: the Central Plateau edged by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">Great Escarpment</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Fold_Belt" title="Cape Fold Belt">Cape Fold Belt</a> in the south-west corner of the country</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1394" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png/300px-Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png/450px-Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png/600px-Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_South_Africa_1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Important geographical regions in South Africa. The thick line traces the course of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">Great Escarpment</a> which edges the central plateau. The eastern portion of this line, coloured red, is known as the <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a>. The Escarpment rises to its highest point, at over 3,000&#160;m (9,800&#160;ft), where the Drakensberg forms the border between <a href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal" title="KwaZulu-Natal">KwaZulu-Natal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>. None of the regions indicated on the map has a sharp well-defined border, except where the Escarpment or a range of mountains forms a clear dividing line between two regions. Some of the better known regions are coloured in; the others are simply indicated by their names, as they would be in an atlas</div></div></div>\n<p>South Africa is located at the southernmost region of Africa, with a long coastline that stretches more than 2,500&#160;km (1,553&#160;mi) and along two oceans (the South Atlantic and the Indian). At 1,219,912&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (471,011&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> according to the UN Demographic Yearbook,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> South Africa is the 25th-largest country in the world. It is about the same size as <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, twice the size of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, three times as big as <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, four times the size of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and five times the size of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mafadi" title="Mafadi">Mafadi</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a> at 3,450&#160;m (11,320&#160;ft) is the highest peak in South Africa. Excluding the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Islands" title="Prince Edward Islands">Prince Edward Islands</a>, the country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/22nd_parallel_south" title="22nd parallel south">22&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/35th_parallel_south" title="35th parallel south">35&#176;S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/16th_meridian_east" title="16th meridian east">16&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/33rd_meridian_east" title="33rd meridian east">33&#176;E</a>.\n</p><p>The interior of South Africa consists of a vast, in most places almost flat, plateau with an altitude of between 1,000&#160;m (3,300&#160;ft) and 2,100&#160;m (6,900&#160;ft), highest in the east and sloping gently downwards towards the west and north, and slightly less noticeably so to the south and south-west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> This plateau is surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">Great Escarpment</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altas_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altas-79">[78]</a></sup> whose eastern, and highest, stretch is known as the <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The south and south-western parts of the plateau (at approximately 1100&#8211;1800<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m above sea level), and the adjoining plain below (at approximately 700&#8211;800<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m above sea level&#160;&#8211;&#160;see map on the right) is known as the <a href="/wiki/Karoo" title="Karoo">Great Karoo</a>, which consists of sparsely populated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scrubland" title="Scrubland">scrubland</a>. To the north the Great Karoo fades into the even drier and more arid Bushmanland, which eventually becomes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalahari" title="Kalahari">Kalahari</a> desert in the very north-west of the country. The mid-eastern, and highest part of the plateau is known as the <a href="/wiki/Highveld" title="Highveld">Highveld</a>. This relatively well-watered area is home to a great proportion of the country\'s commercial farmlands, and contains its largest conurbation (Gauteng). To the north of Highveld, from about the 25&#176;<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>30\'<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>S line of latitude, the plateau slopes downwards into the <a href="/wiki/Bushveld" title="Bushveld">Bushveld</a>, which ultimately gives way to the Limpopo lowlands or <a href="/wiki/Veld#Highveld_and_Lowveld" title="Veld">Lowveld</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altas_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Altas-79">[78]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karoo_Koppies.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1148" data-file-width="4160" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Karoo_Koppies.png/440px-Karoo_Koppies.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Karoo_Koppies.png/660px-Karoo_Koppies.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Karoo_Koppies.png/880px-Karoo_Koppies.png 2x" width="440"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karoo_Koppies.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flat topped hills (called Karoo <i>Koppies</i>) are highly characteristic of the southern and southwestern <a href="/wiki/Karoo" title="Karoo">Karoo</a> landscape. These hills are capped by hard, erosion resistant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dolerite" title="Dolerite">dolerite</a> <a href="/wiki/Sill_(geology)" title="Sill (geology)">sills</a>. This is solidified lava that was forced under high pressure between the horizontal <a href="/wiki/Stratum" title="Stratum">strata</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a> that make up most of the <a href="/wiki/Karoo_Supergroup" title="Karoo Supergroup">Karoo\'s geology</a> about 180<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million years ago. Since then, Southern Africa has undergone a prolonged period of erosion removing the relatively soft Karoo rocks, except where they are protected by a cap of dolerite. This photograph was taken near <a href="/wiki/Cradock,_Eastern_Cape" title="Cradock, Eastern Cape">Cradock</a> in the Eastern Cape</div></div></div>\n<p>The coastal belt, below the Great Escarpment, moving clockwise from the northeast, consists of the Limpopo Lowveld, which merges into the Mpumalanga Lowveld, below the Mpumalanga Drakensberg (the eastern portion of the Great Escarpment).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> This is hotter, drier and less intensely cultivated than the Highveld above the escarpment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altas_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-Altas-79">[78]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kruger_National_Park" title="Kruger National Park">Kruger National Park</a>, located in the provinces of Limpopo and Mpumalanga in northeastern South Africa, occupies a large portion of the Lowveld covering 19,633 square kilometres (7,580 sq mi.) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kruger_National_Park_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kruger_National_Park-82">[81]</a></sup> South of the Lowveld the annual rainfall increases as one enters KwaZulu-Natal Province, which, especially near the coast, is <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropically</a> hot and humid. The KwaZulu-Natal&#8211;Lesotho international border is formed by the highest portion of the Great Escarpment, or Drakensberg, which reaches an altitude of over 3,000&#160;m (9,800&#160;ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> The climate at the foot of this part of the Drakensberg is temperate.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_(16261357780).jpg"><img alt="Image depicting the Drakensberg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2989" data-file-width="5313" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_%2816261357780%29.jpg/220px-South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_%2816261357780%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_%2816261357780%29.jpg/330px-South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_%2816261357780%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_%2816261357780%29.jpg/440px-South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_%2816261357780%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_-_Drakensberg_(16261357780).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a>, the eastern and highest portion of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">Great Escarpment</a> which surrounds the east, south and western borders of the central plateau of Southern Africa</div></div></div>\n<p>The coastal belt below the south and south-western stretches of the Great Escarpment contains several ranges of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Fold_Belt" title="Cape Fold Belt">Cape Fold Mountains</a> which run parallel to the coast, separating the Great Escarpment from the ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geological_map_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-geological_map-85">[84]</a></sup> (These parallel ranges of fold mountains are shown on the map, above left. Note the course of the Great Escarpment to the north of these mountain ranges.) The land (at approximately 400&#8211;500<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m above sea level) between two of these ranges of fold mountains in the south (i.e. between the <a href="/wiki/Outeniqua_Mountains" title="Outeniqua Mountains">Outeniqua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Langeberg" title="Langeberg">Langeberg</a> ranges to the south and the <a href="/wiki/Swartberg" title="Swartberg">Swartberg</a> range to the north) is known as the <a href="/wiki/Karoo" title="Karoo">Little Karoo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altas_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-Altas-79">[78]</a></sup> which consists of semi-desert scrubland similar to that of the Great Karoo, except that its northern strip along the foothills of the Swartberg Mountains, has a somewhat higher rainfall and is therefore more cultivated than the Great Karoo. The Little Karoo is historically, and still, famous for its <a href="/wiki/Ostrich" title="Ostrich">ostrich</a> farming around the town of <a href="/wiki/Oudtshoorn" title="Oudtshoorn">Oudtshoorn</a>. The lowland area (700&#8211;800<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m above sea level) to the north of the Swartberg mountain range up to the Great Escarpment is the lowland part of the Great Karoo (see map at top right), which is climatically and botanically almost indistinguishable from the Karoo above the Great Escarpment. The narrow coastal strip between the most seaward Cape Fold Mountain range (i.e., the Langeberg&#8211;Outeniqua mountains) and the ocean has a moderately high year-round rainfall, especially in the <a href="/wiki/George,_Western_Cape" title="George, Western Cape">George</a>-<a href="/wiki/Knysna" title="Knysna">Knysna</a>-<a href="/wiki/Plettenberg_Bay" title="Plettenberg Bay">Plettenberg Bay</a> region, which is known as the <a href="/wiki/Garden_Route" title="Garden Route">Garden Route</a>. It is famous for the most extensive areas of indigenous forests in South Africa (a generally forest-poor country).\n</p><p>In the south-west corner of the country, the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Peninsula" title="Cape Peninsula">Cape Peninsula</a> forms the southernmost tip of the coastal strip which borders the Atlantic Ocean, and ultimately terminates at the country\'s border with Namibia at the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Peninsula" title="Cape Peninsula">Cape Peninsula</a> has a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a>, making it and its immediate surrounds the only portion of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Africa south of the Sahara</a> which receives most of its rainfall in winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altas1_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altas1-87">[86]</a></sup> The greater <a href="/wiki/City_of_Cape_Town" title="City of Cape Town">Cape Town metropolitan area</a> is situated on the Cape Peninsula and is home to 3.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million people according to the 2011 population census. It is the country\'s legislative capital.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namaqualand,_Goegap_0035.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Namaqualand%2C_Goegap_0035.jpg/220px-Namaqualand%2C_Goegap_0035.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Namaqualand%2C_Goegap_0035.jpg/330px-Namaqualand%2C_Goegap_0035.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Namaqualand%2C_Goegap_0035.jpg/440px-Namaqualand%2C_Goegap_0035.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namaqualand,_Goegap_0035.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spring flowers in <a href="/wiki/Namaqualand" title="Namaqualand">Namaqualand</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The coastal belt to the north of the Cape Peninsula is bounded on the west by the Atlantic Ocean and the first row of north-south running Cape Fold Mountains to the east. The Cape Fold Mountains peter out at about the 32&#176;<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>S line of latitude,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geological_map_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-geological_map-85">[84]</a></sup> after which the coastal plain is bounded by the Great Escarpment itself. The most southerly portion of this coastal belt is known as the <a href="/wiki/Swartland" title="Swartland">Swartland</a> and Malmesbury Plain, which is an important wheat growing region, relying on winter rains. The region further north is known as <a href="/wiki/Namaqualand" title="Namaqualand">Namaqualand</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> which becomes more and more arid as one approaches the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a>. The little rain that falls, tends to fall in winter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altas1_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Altas1-87">[86]</a></sup> which results in one of the world\'s most spectacular displays of flowers carpeting huge stretches of <i><a href="/wiki/Veld" title="Veld">veld</a></i> in spring (August&#8211;September).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg/220px-Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg/330px-Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg/440px-Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas" title="Cape Floral Region Protected Areas">Cape Floral Region Protected Areas</a></div></div></div>\n<p>South Africa also has one possession, the small <a href="/wiki/Subantarctic" title="Subantarctic">sub-Antarctic</a> <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of the Prince Edward Islands, consisting of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marion_Island" title="Marion Island">Marion Island</a> (290&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 110&#160;sq&#160;mi) and Prince Edward Island (45&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 17&#160;sq&#160;mi) (not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Canadian province of the same name</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_South_Africa" title="Climate of South Africa">Climate of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1287" data-file-width="1080" decoding="async" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/220px-South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/330px-South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/440px-South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen climate types</a> of South Africa</div></div></div>\n<p>South Africa has a generally <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climate</a>, due in part to being surrounded by the Atlantic and Indian Oceans on three sides, by its location in the climatically milder <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> and due to the average elevation rising steadily towards the north (towards the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>) and further inland. Due to this varied topography and oceanic influence, a great variety of climatic zones exist. The climatic zones range from the extreme desert of the southern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" title="Namib Desert">Namib</a> in the farthest northwest to the lush subtropical climate in the east along the border with Mozambique and the Indian Ocean. Winters in South Africa occur between June and August.\n</p><p>The extreme southwest has a climate remarkably similar to that of the Mediterranean with wet winters and hot, dry summers, hosting the famous <a href="/wiki/Fynbos" title="Fynbos">fynbos</a> <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biome</a> of <a href="/wiki/Shrubland" title="Shrubland">shrubland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albany_thickets" title="Albany thickets">thicket</a>. This area also produces much of the wine in South Africa. This region is also particularly known for its wind, which blows intermittently almost all year. The severity of this wind made passing around the Cape of Good Hope particularly treacherous for sailors, causing many shipwrecks. Further east on the south coast, rainfall is distributed more evenly throughout the year, producing a green landscape. This area is popularly known as the <a href="/wiki/Garden_Route" title="Garden Route">Garden Route</a>.\n</p><p>The Free State is particularly flat because it lies centrally on the high plateau. North of the <a href="/wiki/Vaal_River" title="Vaal River">Vaal River</a>, the Highveld becomes better watered and does not experience subtropical extremes of heat. Johannesburg, in the centre of the Highveld, is at 1,740&#160;m (5,709&#160;ft) above sea level and receives an annual rainfall of 760&#160;mm (29.9&#160;in). Winters in this region are cold, although snow is rare.\n</p><p>The high Drakensberg mountains, which form the south-eastern escarpment of the Highveld, offer limited skiing opportunities in winter. The coldest place on mainland South Africa is <a href="/wiki/Sutherland,_Northern_Cape" title="Sutherland, Northern Cape">Sutherland</a> in the western <a href="/wiki/Roggeveld_Mountains" title="Roggeveld Mountains">Roggeveld Mountains</a>, where midwinter temperatures can reach as low as &#8722;15&#160;&#176;C (5&#160;&#176;F). The Prince Edward Islands have colder average annual temperatures, but Sutherland has colder extremes. The deep interior of mainland South Africa has the hottest temperatures: a temperature of 51.7&#160;&#176;C (125.06&#160;&#176;F) was recorded in 1948 in the Northern Cape Kalahari near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upington,_Northern_Cape" title="Upington, Northern Cape">Upington</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> but this temperature is unofficial and was not recorded with standard equipment, the official highest temperature is 48.8&#160;&#176;C (119.84&#160;&#176;F) at <a href="/wiki/Vioolsdrif" title="Vioolsdrif">Vioolsdrif</a> in January 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_South_Africa" title="Wildlife of South Africa">Wildlife of South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_South_Africa" title="Protected areas of South Africa">Protected areas of South Africa</a></div>\n<p>South Africa signed the Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> on 4 June 1994, and became a party to the convention on 2 November 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> It has subsequently produced a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_action_plan" title="Biodiversity action plan">National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan</a>, which was received by the convention on 7 June 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbd.int_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbd.int-92">[91]</a></sup> The country is ranked sixth out of the world\'s seventeen <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_African_Giraffes,_fighting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1370" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg/220px-South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg/330px-South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg/440px-South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_African_Giraffes,_fighting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/South_African_giraffe" title="South African giraffe">South African giraffe</a>, Kruger National Park</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:African_buffalo_(Syncerus_caffer)_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg"><img alt="African buffalo (Syncerus caffer) male with red-billed oxpecker (Buphagus erythrorhynchus), Phinda Private Game Reserve, KwaZulu Natal, South Africa" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3499" data-file-width="4265" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/African_buffalo_%28Syncerus_caffer%29_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg/220px-African_buffalo_%28Syncerus_caffer%29_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/African_buffalo_%28Syncerus_caffer%29_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg/330px-African_buffalo_%28Syncerus_caffer%29_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/African_buffalo_%28Syncerus_caffer%29_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg/440px-African_buffalo_%28Syncerus_caffer%29_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:African_buffalo_(Syncerus_caffer)_male_with_Oxpecker.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/African_buffalo" title="African buffalo">African buffalo</a> (<i>Syncerus caffer</i>) male with <a href="/wiki/Red-billed_oxpecker" title="Red-billed oxpecker">red-billed oxpecker</a> (<i>Buphagus erythrorhynchus</i>), <a href="/wiki/Phinda_Private_Game_Reserve" title="Phinda Private Game Reserve">Phinda Private Game Reserve</a>, KwaZulu Natal, South Africa</div></div></div>\n<p>Numerous mammals are found in the <a href="/wiki/Bushveld" title="Bushveld">Bushveld</a> including <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_leopard" title="African leopard">African leopards</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_cheetah" title="South African cheetah">South African cheetahs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_white_rhino" title="Southern white rhino">southern white rhinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_wildebeest" title="Blue wildebeest">blue wildebeest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kudu" title="Kudu">kudus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Impala" title="Impala">impalas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyena" title="Hyena">hyenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus">hippopotamuses</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_African_giraffe" title="South African giraffe">South African giraffes</a>. A significant extent of the Bushveld exists in the north-east including <a href="/wiki/Kruger_National_Park" title="Kruger National Park">Kruger National Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sabi_Sand_Game_Reserve" title="Sabi Sand Game Reserve">Sabi Sand Game Reserve</a>, as well as in the far north in the <a href="/wiki/Waterberg_Biosphere" title="Waterberg Biosphere">Waterberg Biosphere</a>. South Africa houses many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endemic_species" title="Endemic species">endemic species</a>, among them the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Riverine_rabbit" title="Riverine rabbit">riverine rabbit</a> (<i>Bunolagus monticullaris</i>) in the Karoo.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fungi">Fungi</span></h4>\n<p>Up to 1945, more than 4900 species of <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Lichen#Fungi" title="Lichen">lichen-forming</a> species) had been recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> In 2006, the number of fungi in South Africa was estimated at about 200,000 species, but did not take into account fungi associated with insects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> If correct, then the number of South African fungi dwarfs that of its plants. In at least some major South African ecosystems, an exceptionally high percentage of fungi are highly specific in terms of the plants with which they occur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> The country\'s Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan does not mention fungi (including lichen-forming fungi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbd.int_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-cbd.int-92">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants">Plants</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2988" data-file-width="5312" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg/220px-Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg/330px-Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg/440px-Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Subtropical forest near <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KNP_Landscape.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2988" data-file-width="5312" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KNP_Landscape.jpg/220px-KNP_Landscape.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KNP_Landscape.jpg/330px-KNP_Landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KNP_Landscape.jpg/440px-KNP_Landscape.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KNP_Landscape.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lowveld" title="Lowveld">Lowveld</a> vegetation of the <a href="/wiki/Kruger_National_Park" title="Kruger National Park">Kruger National Park</a></div></div></div>\n<p>With more than 22,000 different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higher_plants" title="Higher plants">higher plants</a>, or about 9% of all the known species of plants on Earth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> South Africa is particularly rich in plant diversity. The most prevalent biome in South Africa is the <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grassland</a>, particularly on the Highveld, where the plant cover is dominated by different <a href="/wiki/Poaceae" title="Poaceae">grasses</a>, low <a href="/wiki/Shrub" title="Shrub">shrubs</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acacia_tree" title="Acacia tree">acacia trees</a>, mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camelthorn_tree" title="Camelthorn tree">camel-thorn</a> (<i>Vachellia erioloba</i>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whitethorn_acacia" title="Whitethorn acacia">whitethorn</a> (<i>V. constricta</i>). Vegetation becomes even more sparse towards the northwest due to low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">rainfall</a>. There are several species of water-storing <a href="/wiki/Succulent_plant" title="Succulent plant">succulents</a>, like <a href="/wiki/Aloe" title="Aloe">aloes</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euphorbias" title="Euphorbias">euphorbias</a>, in the very hot and dry Namaqualand area. The grass and thorn <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savannah" title="Savannah">savannah</a> turns slowly into a bush savannah towards the north-east of the country, with denser growth. There are significant numbers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baobab" title="Baobab">baobab</a> trees in this area, near the northern end of Kruger National Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Fynbos" title="Fynbos">fynbos</a> biome, which makes up the majority of the area and plant life in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_floristic_region" title="Cape floristic region">Cape floristic region</a>, one of the six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Floral_kingdom" title="Floral kingdom">floral kingdoms</a>, is located in a small region of the Western Cape and contains more than 9,000 of those species, making it among the richest regions on earth in terms of plant diversity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Most of the plants are <a href="/wiki/Evergreen" title="Evergreen">evergreen</a> hard-leaf plants with fine, needle-like leaves, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sclerophyllous" title="Sclerophyllous">sclerophyllous</a> plants. Another uniquely South African flowering plant group is the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Protea" title="Protea">Protea</a></i>. There are around 130 different species of Protea in South Africa.\n</p><p>While South Africa has a great wealth of flowering plants, only 1% of South Africa is forest, almost exclusively in the humid <a href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Cape_coastal_forest_mosaic" title="KwaZulu-Cape coastal forest mosaic">coastal plain of KwaZulu-Natal</a>, where there are also areas of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa_mangroves" title="Southern Africa mangroves">Southern Africa mangroves</a> in river mouths. There are even smaller reserves of forests that are out of the reach of fire, known as <a href="/wiki/Knysna-Amatole_montane_forests" title="Knysna-Amatole montane forests">montane forests</a>. Plantations of imported tree species are predominant, particularly the non-native <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_issues">Conservation issues</span></h3>\n<p>South Africa has lost a large area of natural habitat in the last four decades, primarily due to overpopulation, sprawling development patterns and deforestation during the 19th century. South Africa is one of the worst affected countries in the world when it comes to invasion by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alien_species" title="Alien species">alien species</a> with many (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Acacia_mearnsii" title="Acacia mearnsii">black wattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acacia_saligna" title="Acacia saligna">Port Jackson willow</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hakea" title="Hakea">Hakea</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lantana" title="Lantana">Lantana</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jacaranda" title="Jacaranda">Jacaranda</a></i>) posing a significant threat to the native biodiversity and the already scarce water resources. The original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests">temperate forest</a> found by the first European settlers was exploited ruthlessly until only small patches remained. Currently, South African <a href="/wiki/Hardwood" title="Hardwood">hardwood</a> trees like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_yellowwood" title="Real yellowwood">real yellowwood</a> (<i>Podocarpus latifolius</i>), <a href="/wiki/Ocotea_bullata" title="Ocotea bullata">stinkwood</a> (<i>Ocotea bullata</i>), and South African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olea_laurifolia" title="Olea laurifolia">black ironwood</a> (<i>Olea laurifolia</i>) are under government protection. Statistics from the South African <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Environmental_Affairs" title="Department of Environmental Affairs">Department of Environmental Affairs</a> show a record 1,215 rhinos have been killed in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> is expected to bring considerable warming and drying to much of this already <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-arid_region" title="Semi-arid region">semi-arid region</a>, with greater frequency and intensity of extreme weather events such as <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heat waves</a>, flooding and drought. According to computer-generated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_modelling" title="Climate modelling">climate modelling</a> produced by the South African National Biodiversity Institute,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SANBI_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-SANBI-100">[99]</a></sup> parts of southern Africa will see an increase in temperature by about 1&#160;&#176;C (1.8&#160;&#176;F) along the coast to more than 4&#160;&#176;C (7.2&#160;&#176;F) in the already hot <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a> such as the Northern Cape in late spring and summertime by 2050. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Floral_Kingdom" title="Cape Floral Kingdom">Cape Floral Kingdom</a>, being identified as one of the global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspots" title="Biodiversity hotspots">biodiversity hotspots</a>, will be hit very hard by climate change. Drought, increased intensity and frequency of fire, and climbing temperatures are expected to push many rare species towards extinction.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tnone center"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:642px;max-width:642px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Biodiversity of South Africa</div><div class="tsingle" href="/wiki/Protea_cynaroides" title="Protea cynaroides">King protea</a>, national flower</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fynbos.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="120"
