//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Fynbos.jpg/320px-Fynbos.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Fynbos" title="Fynbos">Fynbos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Floristic_Region" title="Cape Floristic Region">Cape Floristic Region</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:175px;max-width:175px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blue_crane_SA.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2339" data-file-width="3371" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Blue_crane_SA.jpg/173px-Blue_crane_SA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Blue_crane_SA.jpg/260px-Blue_crane_SA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Blue_crane_SA.jpg/346px-Blue_crane_SA.jpg 2x" width="173"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Blue_crane" title="Blue crane">Blue crane</a>, national bird</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Weskus_Nasionale_Park.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="390" data-file-width="520" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Weskus_Nasionale_Park.jpg/160px-Weskus_Nasionale_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Weskus_Nasionale_Park.jpg/240px-Weskus_Nasionale_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Weskus_Nasionale_Park.jpg/320px-Weskus_Nasionale_Park.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Flowers in the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_National_Park" title="West Coast National Park">West Coast National Park</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_South_Africa" title="Government of South Africa">Government of South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_South_Africa" title="Politics of South Africa">Politics of South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_of_South_Africa" title="Law of South Africa">Law of South Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_South_Africa" title="Human rights in South Africa">Human rights in South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uniegebou.jpg"><img alt="Photo of the Union Buildings" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="787" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Uniegebou.jpg/220px-Uniegebou.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Uniegebou.jpg/330px-Uniegebou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Uniegebou.jpg/440px-Uniegebou.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uniegebou.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Union_Buildings" title="Union Buildings">Union Buildings</a> in Pretoria, seat of the executive</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houses_of_Parliament_(Cape_Town).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1893" data-file-width="2274" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg/220px-Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg/330px-Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg/440px-Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houses_of_Parliament_(Cape_Town).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Houses of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa" title="Parliament of South Africa">Parliament</a> in Cape Town, seat of the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a></div></div></div>\n<p>South Africa is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, although unlike most such republics the <a href="/wiki/President_of_South_Africa" title="President of South Africa">President</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and depends for his tenure on the <a href="/wiki/Confidence_and_supply" title="Confidence and supply">confidence</a> of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa" title="Parliament of South Africa">Parliament</a>. The executive, legislature and judiciary are all subject to the supremacy of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_South_Africa" title="Courts of South Africa">superior courts</a> have the power to strike down executive actions and acts of Parliament if they are unconstitutional.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_South_Africa" title="National Assembly of South Africa">National Assembly</a>, the lower house of Parliament, consists of 400 members and is elected every five years by a system of <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Provinces" title="National Council of Provinces">National Council of Provinces</a>, the upper house, consists of ninety members, with each of the nine <a href="/wiki/Provincial_legislature_(South_Africa)" title="Provincial legislature (South Africa)">provincial legislatures</a> electing ten members.\n</p><p>After each parliamentary election, the National Assembly elects one of its members as President; hence the President serves a term of office the same as that of the Assembly, normally five years. No President may serve more than two terms in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> The President appoints a <a href="/wiki/Deputy_President_of_South_Africa" title="Deputy President of South Africa">Deputy President</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">Ministers</a>, who form the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_South_Africa" title="Cabinet of South Africa">Cabinet</a> which consists of <a href="/wiki/Departmentalization" title="Departmentalization">Departments</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_(government_department)" title="Ministry (government department)">Ministries</a>. The President and the Cabinet may be removed by the National Assembly by a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">motion of no confidence</a>.\n</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_general_election,_2014" title="South African general election, 2014">most recent election</a>, held on 7 May 2014, the ANC won 62.2% of the vote and 249 seats, while the main opposition, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Alliance_(South_Africa)" title="Democratic Alliance (South Africa)">Democratic Alliance</a> (DA) won 22.2% of the vote and 89 seats. The <a href="/wiki/Economic_Freedom_Fighters" title="Economic Freedom Fighters">Economic Freedom Fighters</a> (EFF), founded by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Malema" title="Julius Malema">Julius Malema</a>, the former President of the ANC\'s Youth Wing (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ANC_Youth_League" title="ANC Youth League">ANC Youth League</a>) who was later expelled from the ANC, won 6.4% of the vote and 25 seats. The ANC has been the governing political party in South Africa since the end of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>.\n</p><p>South Africa has no legally defined capital city. The fourth chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution of South Africa</a>, states that "The seat of Parliament is Cape Town, but an Act of Parliament enacted in accordance with section 76(1) and (5) may determine that the seat of Parliament is elsewhere."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> The country\'s three branches of government are split over different cities. <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, as the seat of Parliament, is the legislative capital; <a href="/wiki/Pretoria" title="Pretoria">Pretoria</a>, as the seat of the President and Cabinet, is the administrative capital; and <a href="/wiki/Bloemfontein" title="Bloemfontein">Bloemfontein</a>, as the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Appeal_of_South_Africa" title="Supreme Court of Appeal of South Africa">Supreme Court of Appeal</a>, is the judicial capital, while the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Constitutional Court of South Africa">Constitutional Court of South Africa</a> sits in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>. Most foreign embassies are located in Pretoria.\n</p><p>Since 2004, South Africa has had many thousands of popular protests, some violent, making it, according to one academic, the "most protest-rich country in the world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> There have been a number of incidents of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_repression_in_post-Apartheid_South_Africa" title="Political repression in post-Apartheid South Africa">political repression</a> as well as threats of future repression in violation of the constitution, leading some analysts and <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a> organisations to conclude that there is or could be a new climate of political repression,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> or a decline in political tolerance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, South Africa placed 5th out of 48 <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan African</a> countries on the <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>. South Africa scored well in the categories of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rule_of_Law" title="Rule of Law">Rule of Law</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transparency_(social)" title="Transparency (social)">Transparency</a> &amp; Corruption, and <a href="/wiki/Participation_(decision_making)" title="Participation (decision making)">Participation</a> &amp; Human Rights, but was let down by its relatively poor performance in Safety &amp; Security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> In November 2006, South Africa became the first African country to legalise <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_South_Africa" title="Crime in South Africa">Crime in South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg"><img alt="Photo of the Constitutional Court" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="2496" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg/220px-ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg/330px-ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg/440px-ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Constitutional Court of South Africa">Constitutional Court</a> in Johannesburg</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution of South Africa</a> is the supreme <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> in the country. The primary sources of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_law" title="South African law">South African law</a> are <a href="/wiki/Roman-Dutch_law" title="Roman-Dutch law">Roman-Dutch mercantile law</a> and personal law with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Common_law" title="English Common law">English Common law</a>, as imports of Dutch settlements and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_colonialism" title="British colonialism">British colonialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> The first European based law in South Africa was brought by the Dutch East India Company and is called Roman-Dutch law. It was imported before the <a href="/wiki/Codification_(law)" title="Codification (law)">codification</a> of European law into the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a> and is comparable in many ways to <a href="/wiki/Scots_law" title="Scots law">Scots law</a>. This was followed in the 19th century by <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English law</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common</a> and <a href="/wiki/Statutory_law" title="Statutory law">statutory</a>. After unification in 1910, South Africa had its own parliament which passed laws specific for South Africa, building on those previously passed for the individual member colonies.\n</p><p>The judicial system consists of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magistrates%27_Courts_of_South_Africa" title="Magistrates\' Courts of South Africa">magistrates\' courts</a>, which hear lesser criminal cases and smaller civil cases; the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_South_Africa" title="High Court of South Africa">High Court</a>, which has divisions that serve as the courts of <a href="/wiki/General_jurisdiction" title="General jurisdiction">general jurisdiction</a> for specific areas; the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Appeal_of_South_Africa" title="Supreme Court of Appeal of South Africa">Supreme Court of Appeal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Constitutional Court of South Africa">Constitutional Court</a>, which is the highest court.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dying_For_Justice_(8036294736).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg/220px-Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg/330px-Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg/440px-Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dying_For_Justice_(8036294736).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soweto Pride 2012 participants protest against violence against lesbians. The country has strong human rights laws but some groups are still discriminated against. It is the first country in Africa to recognise <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Same_sex_marriage" title="Same sex marriage">same sex marriage</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Nearly 50 murders are committed each day in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> In the year ended March 2014, there were 17,068 murders and the murder rate was 32.2 per 100,000 &#8211; about five times higher than the global average of 6 per 100,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Middle-class South Africans seek security in <a href="/wiki/Gated_community" title="Gated community">gated communities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Private_security_industry_in_South_Africa" title="Private security industry in South Africa">private security industry in South Africa</a> is the largest in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> with nearly 9,000 registered companies and 400,000 registered active private security guards, more than the South African police and army combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> Many emigrants from South Africa also state that crime was a major factor in their decision to leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_Farmer_Murders" title="South African Farmer Murders">Crime against the farming community</a> has continued to be a major problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup>\n</p><p>South Africa has a high <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> rate, with 43,195 rapes reported in 2014/15, and an unknown number of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexual assaults</a> going unreported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africaCheckRapeStats_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-africaCheckRapeStats-117">[116]</a></sup> A 2009 survey found one in four South African men admitted to raping someone<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> and another survey found one in three women out of 4,000 surveyed said they had been raped in the past year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-119">[118]</a></sup> Rapes are also perpetrated by children (some as young as ten).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscape_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-medscape-120">[119]</a></sup> The incidence of <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child and infant rape</a> is among the highest in the world, largely as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_cleansing_myth" title="Virgin cleansing myth">virgin cleansing myth</a>, and a number of high-profile cases (sometimes as young as eight months)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscape_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-medscape-120">[119]</a></sup> have outraged the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-time-121">[120]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_South_Africa" title="Foreign relations of South Africa">Foreign relations of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BRICS_leaders_family_photo,_2018_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="1140" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg/220px-BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg/330px-BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg/440px-BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BRICS_leaders_family_photo,_2018_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leaders of the <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a> nations at the <a href="/wiki/10th_BRICS_summit" title="10th BRICS summit">10th BRICS summit</a> in Johannesburg, South Africa, 2018</div></div></div>\n<p>As the Union of South Africa, the country was a founding member of the UN. The then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smuts" title="Jan Smuts">Jan Smuts</a> wrote the <a href="/wiki/Preamble_to_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Preamble to the United Nations Charter">preamble to the UN Charter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gildersleeve_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-gildersleeve-122">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schlesinger_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schlesinger-123">[122]</a></sup> South Africa is one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU), and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of African countries by GDP (nominal)">second largest economy of all the members</a>. It is also a founding member of the AU\'s <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa\'s Development">New Partnership for Africa\'s Development</a> (NEPAD).\n</p><p>South Africa has played a key role as a mediator in African conflicts over the last decade, such as in <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> (DRC), the <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a>, and Zimbabwe. After apartheid ended, South Africa was readmitted to the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. The country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a> and chaired the organisation in 2006. South Africa is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC), <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Peace_and_Cooperation_Zone" title="South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone">South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union" title="Southern African Customs Union">Southern African Customs Union</a> (SACU), <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System" title="Antarctic Treaty System">Antarctic Treaty System</a> (ATS), <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G20_industrial_nations" title="G20 industrial nations">G20</a>, <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Port_Management_Association_of_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa">Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa</a>.\n</p><p>Former South African President <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Jacob Zuma</a> and former Chinese President <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> upgraded bilateral ties between the two countries on 24 August 2010, when they signed the Beijing Agreement, which elevated South Africa\'s earlier "strategic partnership" with China to the higher level of "comprehensive strategic partnership" in both economic and political affairs, including the strengthening of exchanges between their respective ruling parties and legislatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> In April 2011, South Africa formally joined the Brazil-Russia-India-China (<a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a>) grouping of countries, identified by Zuma as the country\'s largest trading partners, and also the largest trading partners with Africa as a whole. Zuma asserted that BRICS member countries would also work with each other through the UN, the Group of Twenty (G20) and the India, Brazil South Africa (IBSA) forum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">South African National Defence Force</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_(8724689015).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg/220px-Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg/330px-Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg/440px-Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_(8724689015).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">SANDF</a> soldiers</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">South African National Defence Force</a> (SANDF) was created in 1994,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution-1993-224_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-1993-224-127">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> as an <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_military" title="Volunteer military">all-volunteer military</a> composed of the former <a href="/wiki/South_African_Defence_Force" title="South African Defence Force">South African Defence Force</a>, the forces of the African nationalist groups (<a href="/wiki/Umkhonto_we_Sizwe" title="Umkhonto we Sizwe">Umkhonto we Sizwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azanian_People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="Azanian People\'s Liberation Army">Azanian People\'s Liberation Army</a>), and the former Bantustan defence forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution-1993-224_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-1993-224-127">[126]</a></sup> The SANDF is subdivided into four branches, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Army" title="South African Army">South African Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Air_Force" title="South African Air Force">South African Air Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Navy" title="South African Navy">South African Navy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Military_Health_Service" title="South African Military Health Service">South African Military Health Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-act-42-2002_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-act-42-2002-129">[128]</a></sup> In recent years, the SANDF has become a major <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> force in Africa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-dod-sep2005-130">[129]</a></sup> and has been involved in operations in Lesotho, the DRC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-dod-sep2005-130">[129]</a></sup> and Burundi,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_130-2"><a href="#cite_note-dod-sep2005-130">[129]</a></sup> amongst others. It has also served in multinational <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Peacekeeping_forces" title="UN Peacekeeping forces">UN peacekeeping forces</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">UN Force Intervention Brigade</a> for example.\n</p><p>South Africa is the only African country to have successfully developed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_South_Africa" title="Nuclear weapons and South Africa">nuclear weapons</a>. It became the first country (followed by <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>) with nuclear capability to voluntarily renounce and dismantle its programme and in the process signed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fas-ocp27_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-fas-ocp27-131">[130]</a></sup> South Africa undertook a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_nuclear_program" title="South African nuclear program">nuclear weapons programme</a> in the 1970s<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fas-ocp27_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-fas-ocp27-131">[130]</a></sup> According to former state president <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FW_de_Klerk" title="FW de Klerk">FW de Klerk</a>, the decision to build a "nuclear deterrent" was taken "as early as 1974 against a backdrop of a <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> expansionist threat."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-132">[131]</a></sup> South Africa is <a href="/wiki/Vela_Incident" title="Vela Incident">alleged to have conducted</a> a nuclear test over the Atlantic in 1979,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> although this is officially denied. Former president, FW de Klerk, maintained that South Africa had "never conducted a clandestine nuclear test."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-132">[131]</a></sup> Six nuclear devices were completed between 1980 and 1990, but all were dismantled before South Africa signed the Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-132">[131]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_South_Africa" title="Provinces of South Africa">Provinces of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="709" data-file-width="809" decoding="async" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg/350px-Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg/525px-Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg/700px-Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_South_Africa" title="Provinces of South Africa">Provinces of South Africa</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Each of the nine provinces is governed by a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Provincial_legislature_(South_Africa)" title="Provincial legislature (South Africa)">legislature</a>, which is elected every five years by <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>. The legislature elects a <a href="/wiki/Premier_(South_Africa)" title="Premier (South Africa)">Premier</a> as head of government, and the Premier appoints an <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_(South_Africa)" title="Executive Council (South Africa)">Executive Council</a> as a provincial cabinet. The powers of provincial governments are limited to topics listed in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution</a>; these topics include such fields as health, education, public housing and transport.\n</p><p>The provinces are in turn divided into 52 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_South_Africa" title="Districts of South Africa">districts</a>: 8 <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_municipality_(South_Africa)" title="Metropolitan municipality (South Africa)">metropolitan</a> and 44 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_municipality_(South_Africa)" title="District municipality (South Africa)">district municipalities</a>. The district municipalities are further subdivided into 226 <a href="/wiki/Local_municipality_(South_Africa)" title="Local municipality (South Africa)">local municipalities</a>. The metropolitan municipalities, which govern the largest urban agglomerations, perform the functions of both district and local municipalities.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" align="left">Kimberley</td>\n<td>372,889</td>\n<td>1,193,780\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a></td>\n<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a></td>\n<td align="left">Cape Town</td>\n<td>129,462</td>\n<td>6,279,730\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;"><a class="image" href="/w/index.php?title=File:Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg&amp;lang=en"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="812" data-file-width="1354" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg/370px-Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg/555px-Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg/740px-Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg.png 2x" width="370"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Per_capita_personal_income" title="Per capita personal income">per capita personal income</a> by race group in South Africa relative to white levels</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_South_Africa" title="Economy of South Africa">Economy of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2168" data-file-width="1429" decoding="async" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg/170px-Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg/255px-Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg/340px-Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/JSE_Limited" title="JSE Limited">Johannesburg Stock Exchange</a> (JSE) is the largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> continent</div></div></div>\n<p>South Africa has a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>, the second largest in Africa after <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. It also has a relatively high <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) per capita compared to other countries in sub-Saharan Africa (US$11,750 at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> as of 2012). Despite this, South Africa is still burdened by a relatively high rate of poverty and unemployment, and is also ranked in the top ten countries in the world for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Income_inequality" title="Income inequality">income inequality</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> measured by the <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a>.\n</p><p>Unlike most of the world\'s poor countries, South Africa does not have a thriving <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a>. Only 15% of South African jobs are in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_sector" title="Informal sector">informal sector</a>, compared with around half in <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">India</a> and nearly three-quarters in <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Indonesia" title="Economy of Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD) attributes this difference to South Africa\'s widespread welfare system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist1_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-economist1-139">[138]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> research shows that South Africa has one of the widest gaps between per capita GDP versus its <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) ranking, with only <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> showing a larger gap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After 1994, government policy brought down <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>, stabilised public finances, and some foreign capital was attracted, however growth was still subpar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assessment2008-2_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-assessment2008-2-141">[140]</a></sup> From 2004 onward, economic growth picked up significantly; both employment and <a href="/wiki/Capital_formation" title="Capital formation">capital formation</a> increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assessment2008-2_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-assessment2008-2-141">[140]</a></sup> During the presidency of Jacob Zuma, the government increased the role of <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprise" title="State-owned enterprise">state-owned enterprises</a> (SOEs). Some of the biggest SOEs are <a href="/wiki/Eskom" title="Eskom">Eskom</a>, the electric power monopoly, <a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">South African Airways</a> (SAA), and <a href="/wiki/Transnet" title="Transnet">Transnet</a>, the railroad and ports monopoly. Some of these SOEs have not been profitable, such as SAA, which has required bailouts totaling R30 billion ($2.25 billion) over 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup>\n</p><p>South Africa is a popular <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_South_Africa" title="Tourism in South Africa">tourist destination</a>, and a substantial amount of revenue comes from tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Principal international trading partners of South Africa&#8212;besides other African countries&#8212;include Germany, the United States, China, Japan, the United Kingdom and Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-144">[143]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_South_Africa" title="Agriculture in South Africa">South African agricultural industry</a> contributes around 10% of formal employment, relatively low compared to other parts of Africa, as well as providing work for casual labourers and contributing around 2.6% of GDP for the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HRW_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-145">[144]</a></sup> Due to the <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">aridity</a> of the land, only 13.5% can be used for crop production, and only 3% is considered high potential land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2013, South Africa was ranked as the top African Country of the Future by <i><a href="/wiki/FDi_magazine" title="FDi magazine">fDi magazine</a></i> based on the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Economic_potential" title="Economic potential">economic potential</a>, labour environment, cost-effectiveness, infrastructure, business friendliness, and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> strategy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Financial_Secrecy_Index" title="Financial Secrecy Index">Financial Secrecy Index</a> (FDI) ranks South Africa as the 50th safest tax haven in the world.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_market">Labour market</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="637" data-file-width="828" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg/220px-Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg/330px-Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg/440px-Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Workers packing pears for export in the <a href="/wiki/Ceres,_Western_Cape" title="Ceres, Western Cape">Ceres Valley</a>, Western Cape</div></div></div>\n<p>During 1995&#8211;2003, the number of formal jobs decreased and informal jobs increased; overall unemployment worsened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sach3_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-sach3-63">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government\'s <a href="/wiki/Black_Economic_Empowerment" title="Black Economic Empowerment">Black Economic Empowerment</a> (BEE) policies have drawn criticism from Neva Makgetla, lead economist for research and information at the <a href="/wiki/Development_Bank_of_Southern_Africa" title="Development Bank of Southern Africa">Development Bank of Southern Africa</a>, for focusing "almost exclusively on promoting individual ownership by black people [which] does little to address broader economic disparities, though the rich may become more diverse."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> Official <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> policies have seen a rise in black economic wealth and an emerging black middle class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> Other problems include <a href="/wiki/State_ownership" title="State ownership">state ownership</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_intervention" title="State intervention">interference</a>, which impose high barriers to entry in many areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assessment2008_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-assessment2008-150">[149]</a></sup> Restrictive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_regulations" title="Labour regulations">labour regulations</a> have contributed to the unemployment malaise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sach3_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-sach3-63">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Along with many African nations, South Africa has been experiencing a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_drain" title="Brain drain">brain drain</a>" in the past 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> and is almost certainly detrimental for the wellbeing of those reliant on the healthcare infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> The skills drain in South Africa tends to demonstrate racial contours given the skills distribution legacy of South Africa and has thus resulted in large white South African communities abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> However, the statistics which purport to show a brain drain are disputed and also do not account for <a href="/wiki/Repatriation" title="Repatriation">repatriation</a> and expiry of foreign work contracts. According to several surveys,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> there has been a reverse in brain drain following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_financial_crisis_of_2008%E2%80%932009" title="Global financial crisis of 2008&#8211;2009">global financial crisis of 2008&#8211;2009</a> and expiration of foreign work contracts. In the first quarter of 2011, confidence levels for graduate professionals were recorded at a level of 84% in a Professional Provident Society (PPS) survey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup>  Illegal immigrants are involved in informal trading.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> Many immigrants to South Africa continue to live in poor conditions, and the immigration policy has become increasingly restrictive since the year 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_South_Africa" title="Science and technology in South Africa">Science and technology in South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="1356" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg/220px-Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg/330px-Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg/440px-Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mark_Shuttleworth" title="Mark Shuttleworth">Mark Shuttleworth</a> in space</div></div></div>\n<p>Several important scientific and technological developments have originated in South Africa. The first human-to-human <a href="/wiki/Heart_transplantation" title="Heart transplantation">heart transplant</a> was performed by cardiac surgeon <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Barnard" title="Christiaan Barnard">Christiaan Barnard</a> at <a href="/wiki/Groote_Schuur_Hospital" title="Groote Schuur Hospital">Groote Schuur Hospital</a> in December 1967, <a href="/wiki/Max_Theiler" title="Max Theiler">Max Theiler</a> developed a <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever_vaccine" title="Yellow fever vaccine">vaccine</a> against <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allan_McLeod_Cormack" title="Allan McLeod Cormack">Allan McLeod Cormack</a> pioneered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-ray_computed_tomography" title="X-ray computed tomography">X-ray computed tomography</a> (CT scan), and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Klug" title="Aaron Klug">Aaron Klug</a> developed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crystallographic_electron_microscopy" title="Crystallographic electron microscopy">crystallographic electron microscopy</a> techniques. With the exception of that of Barnard, all of these advancements were recognised with <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prizes</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Brenner" title="Sydney Brenner">Sydney Brenner</a> won most recently, in 2002, for his pioneering work in <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mark_Shuttleworth" title="Mark Shuttleworth">Mark Shuttleworth</a> founded an early Internet security company <a href="/wiki/Thawte" title="Thawte">Thawte</a>, that was subsequently bought out by world-leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VeriSign" title="VeriSign">VeriSign</a>. Despite government efforts to encourage entrepreneurship in <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, information technology and other high technology fields, no other notable groundbreaking companies have been founded in South Africa. It is the expressed objective of the government to transition the economy to be more reliant on high technology, based on the realisation that South Africa cannot compete with <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far Eastern</a> economies in manufacturing, nor can the republic rely on its mineral wealth in perpetuity.\n</p><p>South Africa has cultivated a burgeoning <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a> community. It hosts the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Large_Telescope" title="Southern African Large Telescope">Southern African Large Telescope</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Optical_telescope" title="Optical telescope">optical telescope</a> in the Southern Hemisphere. South Africa is currently building the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karoo_Array_Telescope" title="Karoo Array Telescope">Karoo Array Telescope</a> as a pathfinder for the &#8364;1.5&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Square_Kilometre_Array" title="Square Kilometre Array">Square Kilometre Array</a> project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> On 25 May 2012, it was announced that hosting of the Square Kilometer Array Telescope will be split over both the South African and the Australia and New Zealand sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-160">[159]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_South_Africa" title="Water supply and sanitation in South Africa">Water supply and sanitation in South Africa</a></div>\n<p>Two distinctive features of the South African water sector are the policy of free basic water and the existence of <a href="/wiki/Water_Board_(South_Africa)" title="Water Board (South Africa)">water boards</a>, which are bulk water supply agencies that operate pipelines and sell water from reservoirs to municipalities. These features have led to significant problems concerning the financial sustainability of service providers, leading to a lack of attention to maintenance. Following the end of apartheid, the country had made improvements in the levels of access to water as those with access increased from 66% to 79% from 1990 to 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMP_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-161">[160]</a></sup> Sanitation access increased from 71% to 79% during the same period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMP_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-161">[160]</a></sup> However, water supply and sanitation in South Africa has come under increasing pressure in recent years despite a commitment made by the government to improve service standards and provide investment subsidies to the water industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The eastern parts of South Africa suffer from periodic <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a> linked to the <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Ni&#241;o">El Ni&#241;o</a> weather phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation-163">[162]</a></sup> In early 2018, Cape Town, which has different weather patterns to the rest of the country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation-163">[162]</a></sup> faced a water crisis as the city\'s water supply was predicted to run dry before the end of June. Water-saving measures were in effect that required each citizen to use less than 50 litres (13&#160;US&#160;gal) a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_South_Africa" title="Demographics of South Africa">Demographics of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="709" data-file-width="809" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg/220px-South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg/330px-South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg/440px-South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_population_density_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of population density in South Africa<div </tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-165">[164]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">13.6\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">45.7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">56\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>South Africa is a nation of about 55 million (2016) people of diverse origins, cultures, languages, and religions. The last <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Census_of_2011" title="South African National Census of 2011">census</a> was held in 2011, with a more recent intercensal national survey conducted in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> South Africa is home to an estimated 5&#160;million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrant" title="Illegal immigrant">illegal immigrants</a>, including some 3&#160;million Zimbabweans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> A series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_South_Africa_riots" title="2008 South Africa riots">anti-immigrant riots</a> occurred in South Africa beginning on 11 May 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-170">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Statistics_South_Africa" title="Statistics South Africa">Statistics South Africa</a> asks people to describe themselves in the census in terms of five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" title="Race (classification of human beings)">racial</a> population groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> The 2011 census figures for these groups were: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_(people)" title="Black (people)">Black African</a> at 79.2%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_South_African" title="White South African">White</a> at 8.9%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coloured" title="Coloured">Coloured</a> at 8.9%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_South_African" title="Asian South African">Asian</a> at 2.5%, and Other/Unspecified at 0.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cib11_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-cib11-6">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>21</span></sup> The first census in South Africa in 1911 showed that whites made up 22% of the population; this had declined to 16% by 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup>\n</p><p>South Africa hosts a sizeable refugee and asylum seeker population. According to the <i>World Refugee Survey 2008</i>, published by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Committee_for_Refugees_and_Immigrants" title="US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants">US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants</a>, this population numbered approximately 144,700 in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-174">[173]</a></sup> Groups of refugees and asylum seekers numbering over 10,000 included people from Zimbabwe (48,400), the DRC (24,800), and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> (12,900).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_174-1"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-174">[173]</a></sup> These populations mainly lived in Johannesburg, Pretoria, <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a>, Cape Town, and <a href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth" title="Port Elizabeth">Port Elizabeth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_174-2"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-174">[173]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">Languages of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="709" data-file-width="809" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg/220px-South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg/330px-South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg/440px-South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the dominant <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">South African languages</a> by area <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #80b1d3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> (22.7%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fb8072; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> (16.0%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8dd3c7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;&#8288;<a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> (13.5%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffffb3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/South_African_English" title="South African English">English</a> (9.6%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fdb462; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Northern_Sotho_language" title="Northern Sotho language">Northern Sotho</a> (9.1%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fccde5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Tswana</a> (8.0%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b3de69; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Sotho_language" title="Sotho language">Southern Sotho</a> (7.6%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffed6f; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">Tsonga</a> (4.5%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #bc80bd; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Swazi_language" title="Swazi language">Swazi</a> (2.5%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ccebc5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Venda_language" title="Venda language">Venda</a> (2.4%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #bebada; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Southern_Ndebele_language" title="Southern Ndebele language">Southern Ndebele</a> (2.1%)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #d0d0d0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;None dominant</div></div></div></div>\n<p>South Africa has 11 official languages:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_African_English" title="South African English">English</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Sotho" title="Northern Sotho">Northern Sotho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Tswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sotho_language" title="Sotho language">Southern Sotho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">Tsonga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swazi_language" title="Swazi language">Swazi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venda_language" title="Venda language">Venda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ndebele_language" title="Southern Ndebele language">Southern Ndebele</a> (in order of first language speakers). In this regard it is fourth only to <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_India" title="Official languages of India">India</a>, and Zimbabwe in number. While all the languages are formally equal, some languages are spoken more than others. According to the 2011 census, the three most spoken first languages are Zulu (22.7%), Xhosa (16.0%), and Afrikaans (13.5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cib11_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-cib11-6">[5]</a></sup> Despite the fact that English is recognised as the language of commerce and science, it is ranked fourth, and was listed as the first language of only 9.6% of South Africans in 2011; but it remains the <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cib11_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-cib11-6">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The country also recognises several unofficial languages, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fanagalo_language" title="Fanagalo language">Fanagalo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khoe_language" title="Khoe language">Khoe</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lobedu_language" title="Lobedu language">Lobedu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">Nama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ndebele_language" title="Northern Ndebele language">Northern Ndebele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phuthi_language" title="Phuthi language">Phuthi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_African_Sign_Language" title="South African Sign Language">South African Sign Language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> These unofficial languages may be used in certain official uses in limited areas where it has been determined that these languages are prevalent.\n</p><p>Many of the unofficial <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">languages of the San and Khoikhoi</a> people contain regional dialects stretching northwards into Namibia and Botswana, and elsewhere. These people, who are a physically distinct population from other Africans, have their own cultural identity based on their <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> societies. They have been marginalised to a great extent, and the remainder of their languages are in danger of becoming <a href="/wiki/Extinct_language" title="Extinct language">extinct</a>.\n</p><p>White South Africans may also speak <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_languages" title="European languages">European languages</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> (also spoken by black <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angolans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambicans</a>), <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, while some Indian South Africans speak <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_India" title="Languages of India">Indian languages</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindi_language" title="Hindi language">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>. <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is spoken in South Africa by migrants from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone_Africa" title="Francophone Africa">Francophone Africa</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_centres">Urban centres</span></h3>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="10"><div style="float:right; width:6em;
