title="Limpopo">Limpopo</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">702,190\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_South_Africa" title="Religion in South Africa">Religion in South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg/220px-Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg/330px-Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg/440px-Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wolmaransstad-NG_Kerk-001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nederduits_Gereformeerde_Kerk" title="Nederduits Gereformeerde Kerk">Nederduits Gereformeerde Kerk</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wolmaransstad" title="Wolmaransstad">Wolmaransstad</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:"><th colspan="5" style="text-align:center;">Religion in South Africa (2010)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">religion</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">percent</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:#B57EDC; width:73.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">73.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">No religion</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:black; width:14.9%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">14.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:darkblue; width:7.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">7.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:green; width:1.7%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:orange; width:1.1%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.1%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other faith</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:silver; width:1.7%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.7%</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to the 2001 census, Christians accounted for 79.8% of the population, with a majority of them being members of various <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">denominations</a> (broadly defined to include <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_initiated_churches" title="African initiated churches">African initiated churches</a>) and a minority of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> and other Christians. Christian category includes <a href="/wiki/Zion_Christian_Church" title="Zion Christian Church">Zion Christian</a> (11.1%), <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charismatic_movement" title="Charismatic movement">Charismatic</a>) (8.2%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_South_Africa" title="Roman Catholicism in South Africa">Roman Catholic</a> (7.1%), <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Southern_Africa" title="Methodist Church of Southern Africa">Methodist</a> (6.8%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nederduits_Gereformeerde_Kerk" title="Nederduits Gereformeerde Kerk">Dutch Reformed</a> (<i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Nederduits Gereformeerde Kerk</i>; 6.7%), and <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Southern_Africa" title="Anglican Church of Southern Africa">Anglican</a> (3.8%). Members of remaining Christian churches accounted for another 36% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_South_Africa" title="Islam in South Africa">Muslims</a> accounted for 1.5% of the population, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_South_Africa" title="Hinduism in South Africa">Hindus</a> 1.2%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-state.gov_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-179">[178]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religion" title="Traditional African religion">traditional African religion</a> 0.3% and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> 0.2%. 15.1% had no religious affiliation, 0.6% were "other" and 1.4% were "unspecified."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-144">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-state.gov_179-1"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-179">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup>\n</p><p>African initiated churches formed the largest of the Christian groups. It was believed that many of the persons who claimed no affiliation with any organised religion adhered to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religion" title="Traditional African religion">traditional African religion</a>. There are an estimated 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Traditional_healers_of_South_Africa" title="Traditional healers of South Africa">indigenous traditional healers</a> in South Africa, and up to 60% of South Africans consult these healers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> generally called <i>sangomas</i> or <i>inyangas</i>. These healers use a combination of <a href="/wiki/Veneration_of_the_dead" title="Veneration of the dead">ancestral spiritual beliefs</a> and a belief in the spiritual and medicinal properties of local fauna and flora, commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_medicine" title="Traditional African medicine"><i>muti</i></a>, to facilitate healing in clients. Many peoples have syncretic religious practices combining Christian and indigenous influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DoS_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-DoS-182">[181]</a></sup>\n</p><p>South African Muslims comprise mainly of those who are described as Coloureds and those who are described as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_South_African" title="Indian South African">Indians</a>. They have been joined by black or white South African <a href="/wiki/Religious_conversion" title="Religious conversion">converts</a> as well as others from other parts of Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csmonitor_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-csmonitor-183">[182]</a></sup> South African Muslims claim that their faith is the fastest-growing religion of conversion in the country, with the number of black Muslims growing sixfold, from 12,000 in 1991 to 74,700 in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csmonitor_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-csmonitor-183">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup>\n</p><p>South Africa is also home to a substantial <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_South_Africa" title="History of the Jews in South Africa">Jewish population</a>, descended from <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Europe" title="History of the Jews in Europe">European Jews</a> who arrived as a minority among other European settlers. This population peaked in the 1970s at 120,000, though only around 67,000 remain today, the rest having emigrated, mostly to <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. Even so, these numbers make the Jewish community in South Africa the twelfth largest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_South_Africa" title="Culture of South Africa">Culture of South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg/220px-SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg/330px-SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg/440px-SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SouthAfricaDecoratedHouses.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Decorated houses, <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The South African black majority still has a substantial number of rural inhabitants who lead largely impoverished lives. It is among these people that cultural traditions survive most strongly; as blacks have become increasingly urbanised and <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Westernised</a>, aspects of traditional culture have declined. Members of the middle class, who are predominantly white but whose ranks include growing numbers of black, coloured and Indian people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> have lifestyles similar in many respects to that of people found in Western Europe, North America and <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Painting,_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1494" data-file-width="2986" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/San_Painting%2C_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG/220px-San_Painting%2C_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/San_Painting%2C_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG/330px-San_Painting%2C_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/San_Painting%2C_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG/440px-San_Painting%2C_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Painting,_Ukalamba_Drakensberge_1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_painting" title="Rock painting">Rock painting</a> of an <a href="/wiki/Common_eland" title="Common eland">eland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/South_African_art" title="South African art">South African art</a> includes the oldest art objects in the world, which were discovered in a South African cave, and dated from 75,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup>\nThe scattered tribes of <a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">Khoisan</a> peoples moving into South Africa from around 10000 BC had their own fluent art styles seen today in a multitude of cave paintings. They were superseded by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a>/<a href="/wiki/Nguni_people" title="Nguni people">Nguni peoples</a> with their own vocabularies of art forms. New forms of art evolved in the mines and townships: a dynamic art using everything from plastic strips to bicycle spokes. The Dutch-influenced folk art of the Afrikaner <a href="/wiki/Trekboer" title="Trekboer"><i>trekboers</i></a> and the urban white artists, earnestly following changing European traditions from the 1850s onwards, also contributed to this eclectic mix which continues to evolve today.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olive_Schreiner.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="349" decoding="async" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Olive_Schreiner.jpg/170px-Olive_Schreiner.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Olive_Schreiner.jpg/255px-Olive_Schreiner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Olive_Schreiner.jpg/340px-Olive_Schreiner.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Olive_Schreiner.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olive_Schreiner" title="Olive Schreiner">Olive Schreiner</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/South_African_literature" title="South African literature">South African literature</a> emerged from a unique social and political history. One of the first well known novels written by a black author in an African language was <a href="/wiki/Sol_Plaatje" title="Sol Plaatje">Solomon Thekiso Plaatje</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Mhudi" title="Mhudi">Mhudi</a></i>, written in 1930. During the 1950s, <i><a href="/wiki/Drum_(South_African_magazine)" title="Drum (South African magazine)">Drum</a></i> magazine became a hotbed of political satire, fiction, and essays, giving a voice to urban black culture.\n</p><p>Notable white South African authors include <a href="/wiki/Alan_Paton" title="Alan Paton">Alan Paton</a>, who published the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Cry,_the_Beloved_Country" title="Cry, the Beloved Country">Cry, the Beloved Country</a></i> in 1948. <a href="/wiki/Nadine_Gordimer" title="Nadine Gordimer">Nadine Gordimer</a> became the first South African to be awarded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Literature" title="Nobel Prize for Literature">Nobel Prize for Literature</a>, in 1991. <a href="/wiki/J._M._Coetzee" title="J. M. Coetzee">JM Coetzee</a> won the Nobel Prize for Literature, in 2003. When awarding the prize, the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Academy" title="Swedish Academy">Swedish Academy</a> stated that Coetzee "in innumerable guises portrays the surprising involvement of the outsider."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Swedish_Academy_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-Swedish_Academy-188">[187]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The plays of <a href="/wiki/Athol_Fugard" title="Athol Fugard">Athol Fugard</a> have been regularly premiered in <a href="/wiki/Fringe_theatre" title="Fringe theatre">fringe theatres</a> in South Africa, London (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Court_Theatre" title="Royal Court Theatre">Royal Court Theatre</a>) and New York. <a href="/wiki/Olive_Schreiner" title="Olive Schreiner">Olive Schreiner</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_an_African_Farm" title="The Story of an African Farm">The Story of an African Farm</a></i> (1883) was a revelation in <a href="/wiki/Victorian_literature" title="Victorian literature">Victorian literature</a>: it is heralded by many as introducing feminism into the novel form.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Breyten_Breytenbach" title="Breyten Breytenbach">Breyten Breytenbach</a> was jailed for his involvement with the guerrilla movement against apartheid. <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Brink" title="Andr&#233; Brink">Andr&#233; Brink</a> was the first Afrikaner writer to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banned_book" title="Banned book">banned</a> by the government after he released the novel <i><a href="/wiki/A_Dry_White_Season" title="A Dry White Season">A Dry White Season</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Media_of_South_Africa" title="Media of South Africa">South African media</a> sector is large, and South Africa is one of Africa\'s major media centres. While South Africa\'s many broadcasters and publications reflect the diversity of the population as a whole, the most commonly used language is English. However, all ten other official languages are represented to some extent or another.\n</p><p>There is great diversity in <a href="/wiki/Music_of_South_Africa" title="Music of South Africa">South African music</a>. Black musicians have developed a unique style called <a href="/wiki/Kwaito" title="Kwaito">Kwaito</a>, that is said to have taken over radio, television, and magazines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup> Of note is <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Fassie" title="Brenda Fassie">Brenda Fassie</a>, who launched to fame with her song "<a href="/wiki/Weekend_Special" title="Weekend Special">Weekend Special</a>", which was sung in English. More famous traditional musicians include <a href="/wiki/Ladysmith_Black_Mambazo" title="Ladysmith Black Mambazo">Ladysmith Black Mambazo</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Soweto_String_Quartet" title="Soweto String Quartet">Soweto String Quartet</a> performs classic music with an African flavour. South Africa has produced world-famous jazz musicians, notably <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Masekela" title="Hugh Masekela">Hugh Masekela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Gwangwa" title="Jonas Gwangwa">Jonas Gwangwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Ibrahim" title="Abdullah Ibrahim">Abdullah Ibrahim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miriam_Makeba" title="Miriam Makeba">Miriam Makeba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Butler" title="Jonathan Butler">Jonathan Butler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_McGregor" title="Chris McGregor">Chris McGregor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sathima_Bea_Benjamin" title="Sathima Bea Benjamin">Sathima Bea Benjamin</a>. Afrikaans music covers multiple genres, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contemporary_music" title="Contemporary music">contemporary</a> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Hofmeyr" title="Steve Hofmeyr">Steve Hofmeyr</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Fokofpolisiekar" title="Fokofpolisiekar">Fokofpolisiekar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Singer-songwriter" title="Singer-songwriter">singer-songwriter</a> <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Loops" title="Jeremy Loops">Jeremy Loops</a>. South African popular musicians that have found international success include <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Clegg" title="Johnny Clegg">Johnny Clegg</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Seether" title="Seether">Seether</a>.\n</p><p>Although few <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_South_Africa" title="Cinema of South Africa">South African film</a> productions are known outside South Africa itself, many foreign films have been produced about South Africa. Arguably, the most high-profile film portraying South Africa in recent years was <i><a href="/wiki/District_9" title="District 9">District 9</a></i>. Other notable exceptions are the film <i><a href="/wiki/Tsotsi" title="Tsotsi">Tsotsi</a></i>, which won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Foreign_Language_Film" title="Academy Award for Foreign Language Film">Academy Award for Foreign Language Film</a> at the <a href="/wiki/78th_Academy_Awards" title="78th Academy Awards">78th Academy Awards</a> in 2006, as well as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U-Carmen_e-Khayelitsha" title="U-Carmen e-Khayelitsha">U-Carmen e-Khayelitsha</a></i>, which won the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bear" title="Golden Bear">Golden Bear</a> at the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="Berlin International Film Festival">Berlin International Film Festival</a>. In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hermanus" title="Oliver Hermanus">Oliver Hermanus</a> film <a href="/wiki/The_Endless_River_(film)" title="The Endless River (film)"><i>The Endless River</i></a> became the first South African film selected for the <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_African_cuisine" title="South African cuisine">South African cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quarter_Mutton_Bunny_Chow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Quarter_Mutton_Bunny_Chow.jpg/220px-Quarter_Mutton_Bunny_Chow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Quarter_Mutton_Bunny_Chow.jpg/330px-Quarter_Mutton_Bunny_Chow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/Quarter_Mutton_Bunny_Chow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quarter_Mutton_Bunny_Chow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of <a href="/wiki/Bunny_chow" title="Bunny chow">bunny chow</a> served in <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a>, originated in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_South_Africans" title="Indian South Africans">Indian South African</a> community<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FromCurries_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FromCurries-190">[189]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>South African cuisine is diverse; foods from many cultures are enjoyed by all and especially marketed to tourists who wish to sample the large variety.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/South_African_cuisine" title="South African cuisine">South African cuisine</a> is heavily meat-based and has spawned the distinctively South African social gathering known as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Braai" title="Braai">braai</a></i>, a variation of the <a href="/wiki/Barbecue" title="Barbecue">barbecue</a>. South Africa has also developed into a major wine producer, with some of the best <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyards</a> lying in valleys around <a href="/wiki/Stellenbosch" title="Stellenbosch">Stellenbosch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franschhoek" title="Franschhoek">Franschhoek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paarl" title="Paarl">Paarl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barrydale" title="Barrydale">Barrydale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_South_Africa" title="Sport in South Africa">Sport in South Africa</a></div>\n<p>South Africa\'s most popular sports are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> Other sports with significant support are swimming, athletics, golf, boxing, tennis, <a href="/wiki/Ringball" title="Ringball">ringball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>. Although soccer commands the greatest following among the youth, other sports like basketball, surfing and skateboarding are increasingly popular.\n</p><p>Soccer players who have played for major foreign clubs include <a href="/wiki/Steven_Pienaar" title="Steven Pienaar">Steven Pienaar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Radebe" title="Lucas Radebe">Lucas Radebe</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philemon_Masinga" title="Philemon Masinga">Philemon Masinga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benni_McCarthy" title="Benni McCarthy">Benni McCarthy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Mokoena" title="Aaron Mokoena">Aaron Mokoena</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delron_Buckley" title="Delron Buckley">Delron Buckley</a>. South Africa hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>, and FIFA president <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Blatter" title="Sepp Blatter">Sepp Blatter</a> awarded South Africa a grade 9 out of 10 for successfully hosting the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Springbok_parade.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Springbok_parade.jpg/220px-Springbok_parade.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Springbok_parade.jpg/330px-Springbok_parade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Springbok_parade.jpg/440px-Springbok_parade.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Springbok_parade.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Springboks" title="Springboks">Springboks</a> in a bus parade after winning the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007 Rugby World Cup</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Famous boxing personalities include Baby Jake <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Matlala" title="Jacob Matlala">Jacob Matlala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vuyani_Bungu" title="Vuyani Bungu">Vuyani Bungu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welcome_Ncita" title="Welcome Ncita">Welcome Ncita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dingaan_Thobela" title="Dingaan Thobela">Dingaan Thobela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerrie_Coetzee" title="Gerrie Coetzee">Gerrie Coetzee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mitchell_(boxer)" title="Brian Mitchell (boxer)">Brian Mitchell</a>. Durban surfer <a href="/wiki/Jordy_Smith" title="Jordy Smith">Jordy Smith</a> won the 2010 Billabong J-Bay Open making him the highest ranked surfer in the world. South Africa produced <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> motor racing\'s 1979 world champion <a href="/wiki/Jody_Scheckter" title="Jody Scheckter">Jody Scheckter</a>. Famous current cricket players include <a href="/wiki/AB_de_Villiers" title="AB de Villiers">AB de Villiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hashim_Amla" title="Hashim Amla">Hashim Amla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dale_Steyn" title="Dale Steyn">Dale Steyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Philander" title="Vernon Philander">Vernon Philander</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Faf_du_Plessis" title="Faf du Plessis">Faf du Plessis</a>; most also participate in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">Indian Premier League</a>.\n</p><p>South Africa has also produced numerous world class rugby players, including <a href="/wiki/Francois_Pienaar" title="Francois Pienaar">Francois Pienaar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joost_van_der_Westhuizen" title="Joost van der Westhuizen">Joost van der Westhuizen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danie_Craven" title="Danie Craven">Danie Craven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frik_du_Preez" title="Frik du Preez">Frik du Preez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naas_Botha" title="Naas Botha">Naas Botha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Habana" title="Bryan Habana">Bryan Habana</a>. South Africa hosted and won the <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby World Cup">1995 Rugby World Cup</a>, and won the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007 Rugby World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_union_team" title="France national rugby union team">France</a>. It followed the 1995 Rugby World Cup by hosting the <a href="/wiki/1996_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1996 African Cup of Nations">1996 African Cup of Nations</a>, with the national team, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Springboks" title="Springboks">Springboks</a>, going on to win the tournament. It also hosted the <a href="/wiki/2003_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2003 Cricket World Cup">2003 Cricket World Cup</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICC_World_Twenty20" title="ICC World Twenty20">2007 World Twenty20 Championship</a>. South Africa\'s national cricket team, the <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_cricket_team" title="South Africa national cricket team">Proteas</a>, has also won the inaugural edition of the <a href="/wiki/1998_ICC_KnockOut_Trophy" title="1998 ICC KnockOut Trophy">1998 ICC KnockOut Trophy</a> by defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indies_national_cricket_team" title="West Indies national cricket team">West Indies</a> in the final. <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_blind_cricket_team" title="South Africa national blind cricket team">South Africa\'s national blind cricket team</a> also went on to win the inaugural edition of the Blind Cricket World Cup in 1998.\n</p><p>In 2004, the swimming team of <a href="/wiki/Roland_Schoeman" title="Roland Schoeman">Roland Schoeman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_Ferns" title="Lyndon Ferns">Lyndon Ferns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darian_Townsend" title="Darian Townsend">Darian Townsend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryk_Neethling" title="Ryk Neethling">Ryk Neethling</a> won the gold medal at the Olympic Games in Athens, simultaneously breaking the world record in the 4&#215;100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freestyle_Relay" title="Freestyle Relay">freestyle relay</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penny_Heyns" title="Penny Heyns">Penny Heyns</a> won Olympic Gold in the 1996 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta_Olympic_Games" title="Atlanta Olympic Games">Atlanta Olympic Games</a>. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Pistorius" title="Oscar Pistorius">Oscar Pistorius</a> became the first double amputee sprinter to compete at the Olympic Games in London. In golf, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Player" title="Gary Player">Gary Player</a> is generally regarded as one of the greatest golfers of all time, having won the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(golf)" title="Grand Slam (golf)">Career Grand Slam</a>, one of five golfers to have done so. Other South African golfers to have won major tournaments include <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Locke" title="Bobby Locke">Bobby Locke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Els" title="Ernie Els">Ernie Els</a>, <a href="/wiki/Retief_Goosen" title="Retief Goosen">Retief Goosen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Clark_(golfer)" title="Tim Clark (golfer)">Tim Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Immelman" title="Trevor Immelman">Trevor Immelman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Oosthuizen" title="Louis Oosthuizen">Louis Oosthuizen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charl_Schwartzel" title="Charl Schwartzel">Charl Schwartzel</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_South_Africa" title="Education in South Africa">Education in South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="747" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg/220px-Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg/330px-Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg/440px-Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mitchells-plain-schoolkids.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Schoolchildren in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitchell%27s_Plain" title="Mitchell\'s Plain">Mitchell\'s Plain</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The adult <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> in 2007 was 88.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescolit_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-194">[193]</a></sup> South Africa has a <a href="/wiki/Three-tier_education" title="Three-tier education">three-tier system</a> of education starting with <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary school</a>, followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high school</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary education</a> in the form of (academic) universities and universities of technology. Learners have twelve years of formal schooling, from grade 1 to 12. Grade R, or grade 0, is a pre-primary foundation year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edufacts0831_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-edufacts0831-195">[194]</a></sup> Primary schools span the first seven years of schooling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> High school education spans a further five years. The <a href="/wiki/National_Senior_Certificate" title="National Senior Certificate">National Senior Certificate</a> (NSC) examination takes place at the end of grade 12 and is necessary for tertiary studies at a <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_South_Africa" title="List of universities in South Africa">South African university</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edufacts0831_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-edufacts0831-195">[194]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Public universities in South Africa are divided into three types: traditional universities, which offer theoretically oriented university degrees; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Technology" title="University of Technology">universities of technology</a> (formerly called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technikon" title="Technikon">technikons</a>"), which offer vocational oriented diplomas and degrees; and comprehensive universities, which offer both types of qualification. There are 23 public universities in South Africa: 11 traditional universities, 6 universities of technology and 6 comprehensive universities.\n</p><p>Under apartheid, schools for black people were subject to discrimination through inadequate funding and a separate syllabus called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_Education_Act" title="Bantu Education Act">Bantu Education</a></i> which was only designed to give them sufficient skills to work as labourers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004, South Africa started reforming its tertiary education system, merging and incorporating small universities into larger institutions, and renaming all tertiary education institutions "university". By 2015, 1.4 million students in higher education have benefited from a financial aid scheme which was promulgated in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cele_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cele-198">[197]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_South_Africa" title="Health in South Africa">Health in South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_South_Africa" title="Healthcare in South Africa">Healthcare in South Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/350px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/525px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/700px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Life expectancy in select Southern African countries, 1960-2012. <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> has caused a fall in life expectancy.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Institute_of_Race_Relations" title="South African Institute of Race Relations">South African Institute of Race Relations</a>, the life expectancy in 2009 was 71 years for a white South African and 48 years for a black South African.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> The healthcare spending in the country is about 9% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smartpl_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-smartpl-200">[199]</a></sup>\n</p><p>About 84% of the population depends on the public healthcare system,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smartpl_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-smartpl-200">[199]</a></sup> which is beset with chronic human resource shortages and limited resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icap_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-icap-201">[200]</a></sup>\n</p><p>About 20% of the population uses private healthcare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fmhealth_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-fmhealth-202">[201]</a></sup> Only 16% of the population is covered by <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">medical aid schemes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medicl_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-medicl-203">[202]</a></sup> The rest pay for private care "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Out-of-pocket_expenses" title="Out-of-pocket expenses">out of pocket</a>" or through in-hospital-only plans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fmhealth_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-fmhealth-202">[201]</a></sup> The three dominant hospital groups, <a href="/wiki/Mediclinic_International" title="Mediclinic International">Mediclinic</a>, <a href="/wiki/LIFE_Healthcare_Group" title="LIFE Healthcare Group">Life Healthcare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netcare" title="Netcare">Netcare</a>, together control 75% of the private hospital market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fmhealth_202-2"><a href="#cite_note-fmhealth-202">[201]</a></sup>\n</p><p>South Africa is home to the third largest hospital in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hani_Baragwanath_Hospital" title="Chris Hani Baragwanath Hospital">Chris Hani Baragwanath Hospital</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="HIV.2FAIDS"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_South_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS in South Africa">HIV/AIDS in South Africa</a></div>\n<p>According to the 2015 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNAIDS" title="UNAIDS">UNAIDS</a> Report, South Africa has an estimated 7 million people living with <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>&#160;&#8211; more than any other country in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> A 2008 study revealed that HIV/AIDS infection in South Africa is distinctly divided along racial lines: 13.6% of blacks are HIV-positive, whereas only 0.3% of whites have the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ten_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-ten-206">[205]</a></sup> Most deaths are experienced by economically active individuals, resulting in many <a href="/wiki/AIDS_orphan" title="AIDS orphan">AIDS orphans</a> who in many cases depend on the state for care and financial support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avertaids_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-avertaids-207">[206]</a></sup> It is estimated that there are 1,200,000 orphans in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avertaids_207-1"><a href="#cite_note-avertaids-207">[206]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The link between HIV, a <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">virus</a> spread primarily by sexual contact, and AIDS was long <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_denial" title="AIDS denial">denied</a> by former president <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">Thabo Mbeki</a> and his health minister <a href="/wiki/Manto_Tshabalala-Msimang" title="Manto Tshabalala-Msimang">Manto Tshabalala-Msimang</a>, who insisted that the many deaths in the country are due to <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition_in_South_Africa" title="Malnutrition in South Africa">malnutrition</a>, and hence poverty, and not HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> In 2007, in response to international pressure, the government made efforts to fight AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.info.gov.za_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.info.gov.za-209">[208]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_general_election,_2009" title="South African general election, 2009">2009 general elections</a>, former president <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Jacob Zuma</a> appointed <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Motsoaledi" title="Aaron Motsoaledi">Dr Aaron Motsoaledi</a> as the new health minister and committed his government to increasing funding for and widening the scope of HIV treatment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> and by 2015, South Africa had made significant progress, with the widespread availability of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-retroviral_drugs" title="Anti-retroviral drugs">antiretroviral drugs</a> resulted in an increase in life expectancy from 52.1 years to 62.5 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conversationHIVExcelled_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-conversationHIVExcelled-211">[210]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div title="Outline of South Africa">Outline of South Africa</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khoi_languages" title="Khoi languages">Khoi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">Nama</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_languages" title="San languages">San</a> languages, <a href="/wiki/South_African_Sign_Language" title="South African Sign Language">South African Sign Language</a>, German, Greek, <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindi_language" title="Hindi language">Hindi</a>, Portuguese, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>, Arabic, <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a> and "other languages used for religious purposes in South Africa" have a special status (<a class="external text" href="http://www.constitutionalcourt.org.za/site/constitution/english-web/ch1.html" Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://www.statssa.gov.za/news_archive/05may2005_1.asp" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on 14 August 2007<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">25 August</span> 2013</span>. <q>Others pointed out that the repeal of the Population Registration Act in 1991 removed any legal basis for specifying \'race\'. The Identification Act of 1997 makes no mention of race. On the other hand, the Employment Equity Act speaks of \'designated groups\' being \'black people, women and people with disabilities\'. The Act defines \'black\' as referring to \'Africans, coloureds and Indians\'. Apartheid and the racial identification which underpinned it explicitly linked race with differential access to resources and power. If the post-apartheid order was committed to remedying this, race would have to be included in surveys and censuses, so that progress in eradicating the consequences of apartheid could be measured and monitored. This was the reasoning that led to a \'self-identifying\' question about \'race\' or \'population group\' in both the 1996 and 2001 population censuses, and in Statistics SA\'s household survey programme.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Business+Report&amp;rft.atitle=Debate+over+race+and+censuses+not+peculiar+to+SA&amp;rft.date=2005-05-05&amp;rft.aulast=Lehohla&amp;rft.aufirst=Pali&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.statssa.gov.za%2Fnews_archive%2F05may2005_1.asp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASouth+Africa"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-173"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-173">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Study Commission on U.S. Policy toward Southern Africa (U.S.) (1981). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=sq43lnbklEUC&amp;pg=PA42" rel="nofollow"><i>South Africa: time running out: the report of the Study Commission on U.S. Policy Toward Southern Africa</i></a>.
